> The Trillion-Dollar Clean Energy Bottleneck: 5 Public Stocks Set to Fuel the Fusion Revolution
>
> The man who lit up the world with the blue LED is about to power it with infinite clean energy.
>
> Nobel Laureate Shuji Nakamura just officially unveiled his groundbreaking plan via Blue Laser Fusion to construct a massive 1-gigawatt laser fusion power plant by 2032.
>
> The Disruptive Fusion Moat Checklist:
>
> 🔹 Lasers Over Magnets: Diverging from legacy magnetic confinement systems, Nakamura is utilizing specialized high-pulse inertial lasers amplified 100,000x via optical cavities to achieve self-sustaining energy net-gain.
>
> 🔹 Zero Radioactive Waste: The platform targets a non-radioactive hydrogen-boron (HB11) fuel cycle—meaning zero harmful neutrons, zero meltdown risks, and absolutely zero long-lived toxic waste.
>
> 🔹 The Ultimate Data Center Solution: As AI hyperscalers exhaust local grids, on-site, baseline, zero-emission laser fusion will become the holy grail infrastructure asset of the next decade.
>
> While Blue Laser Fusion is currently a highly backed private venture (funded by SoftBank, Toyota's SPARX, and Itochu), the massive capital flows pouring into laser hardware, optics, and specialized power electronics are about to trigger a historic multi-billion dollar public supply chain supercycle.
>
> The commercial race for infinite power has officially hit a structural inflection point. Are you positioned for the energy hardware boom, or still chasing speculative applications?
>
> 5 Public Stocks Set to Benefit from the Laser Fusion Boom:
>
> 1. Coherent Corp. (COHR) ⚡What they do / Potential: Manufactures the ultra-high-power industrial laser systems, optics, and precision crystal substrates required to generate and guide hyper-amplified beam pulses into the fusion fuel core.
>
> 2. IPG Photonics Corporation (IPGP) 🔬What they do / Potential: A global pioneer in high-power fiber lasers, uniquely positioned to supply the underlying high-efficiency, multi-kilowatt rapid-firing continuous laser modules necessary to scale up commercial power plants.
>
> 3. L3Harris Technologies, Inc. (LHX) 🛡️What they do / Potential: Builds complex photonic control systems, advanced target tracking tracking arrays, and optical cavities engineered to perfectly time microsecond laser impacts against fusion fuel pellets.
>
> 4. Materion Corporation (MTRN) 🧱What they do / Potential: Supplies advanced high-purity beryllium, specialized alloys, and thermal management metals critical to lining the internal walls of containment chambers to absorb and stabilize intense fusion energy output.
>
> 5. Perma-Fix Environmental Services, Inc. (PESI) ☢️What they do / Potential: While modern laser fusion is exceptionally clean, their specialized nuclear engineering and reactor waste maintenance frameworks will hold primary service value as standard infrastructure protocols roll out.

### 💭 (@euklbe)
_Fri Jul 10 18:10:24 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/euklbe/status/2075643818947608973)

> Q: This seems like a quite complex field to understand.
>
> A: The principle is very similar to urban planning. Frequently used data is placed close by, and occasionally used data is placed further away. Since speed is crucial when data moves, it's the principle of building a customized data transportation network—just like choosing a motorcycle or an express bus depending on the environment. A prime example of a global company specializing in building these communication networks is Broadcom.
>
> Q: To the general public, tech companies might all look similar, but in reality, their unique roles and exclusive technological territories are firmly divided.
>
> A: That's right. The key is to transfer data among HBM, HBF, and GPU as quickly as possible to reduce latency. Currently, data is transmitted as electrical signals through copper wires, but there is a physical limitation where the signal speed drops due to the copper's resistance. To overcome this, the method of transmitting data using 'light' (optical communication) instead of electricity has emerged, which is why silicon photonics-related companies are gaining attention recently. A prime example is the 'InfiniBand' technology acquired by NVIDIA, which handles optical communication between modules. Like the Strait of Hormuz, these monopoly technology companies, holding tight to the bottlenecks in the global chip supply chain, are positioned in their respective fields.
>
> Q: When do you expect HBF to be commercialized?
>
> A: Research is likely progressing with a target of 2027, so I expect the first product to be released around 2028. It is highly likely that one of NVIDIA, AMD, or Google will introduce the first commercialized product. The primary reason Big Tech companies are interested in HBF is to reduce their dependence on Korean companies. If they solely use HBM, they can't escape Samsung Electronics and SK Hynix, but adopting HBF gives them alternatives to collaborate with American companies like SanDisk or Micron.
>
> However, I believe that attempt will ultimately not hold much significance. I argue that to extract the absolute best performance, HBM and HBF must be configured together.
>
> Q: If the environment requires both types of memory, doesn't that create an absolutely advantageous situation for Samsung Electronics and SK Hynix, since they can produce both HBM and HBF?
>
> A: Yes, it does. Because both companies already firmly possess world-class semiconductor stacking and packaging technologies through HBM production, they are naturally bound to hold the upper hand in the next-generation memory competition as well.

### Athu (@athuinvests)
_Fri Jul 10 18:10:36 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 180 · ↻ 16 · 💬 5 · [open on X](https://x.com/athuinvests/status/2075643866481377290)

> Rosenblatt releases bullish report on $AAOI and other optical names before earnings season.
>
> The report cuts through the noise on why the optical sector has been weak the last few weeks. Two main fears stand out, both of which Rosenblatt sees as overstated. 
>
> This looks like a huge buying opportunity.
>
> 1) China InP capacity
>
> > The worry is that Chinese players are ramping hard and will flood the market with cheap lasers, hurting names like $LITE and $COHR.
>
> > Chinese capacity could add 20-40% on top of the 2030 baseline, but supply still falls well short of demand.
>
> > The Chinese are also still behind on the tech. Lower-end lasers are doing fine for 800G and below, but they don’t yet have enough production 200G EMLs for 1.6T+ transceivers or the high-power lasers needed for real CPO scale. 
>
> > Western order books are full through 2027 and into 2028, with $NVDA securing a lot of the supply and $AMD now looking to the same names.
>
> 2) CPO timing
>
> > The early smaller programs remain on track for 2H26 build and 2027 shipments. 
>
> > The bigger scale-up volume looks more likely to hit in 2028, with NPO picking up a lot of the slack in 2027. 
>
> > Other concerns like network flattening from larger switches were already modeled. Exploding XPU demand more than offsets any reduction in transceivers per switch. 
>
> > VCSELs could play a role in some intermediate NPO designs, but high-power InP stays central for flagship CPO performance.
>
> --------------------------------------------------------------
>
> Short sellers: 
>
> - One thing that stood out is what the short sellers are actually saying. Many have been using the China InP story to push the weakness, but most don’t appear to have strong conviction in it. 
> - Multiple shorts told Rosenblatt they plan to close positions ahead of late July and early August earnings and then buy back into optical names in 2027 for the CPO ramp in 2028-2030. 
>
> That’s not something you’d hear if they truly believed the oversupply thesis.
>
> --------------------------------------------------------------
>
> Overall, I feel this is bullish for optical names like $SIVE, $AAOI, $LITE, $COHR, $TSEM, $VIAV, etc. 
>
> It also aligns with what I mentioned before that July end to August start should be a great time for optics as the earnings season plays out and some of this noise clears.
>
> Long photonics!

### Black Hole (@konstructivizm)
_Fri Jul 10 18:22:00 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 78 · ↻ 13 · 💬 5 · [open on X](https://x.com/konstructivizm/status/2075646736484245804)

> Physicists Just Extracted Energy from a “Black Hole” — Without Any Rotation
>
> In 1969, Roger Penrose proposed a mind-bending way to steal energy from a rotating black hole. Drop an object into the ergosphere (the zone just outside the event horizon), let it split, and one piece falls in while the other flies out with more energy than you started with. It sounded like science fiction.
>
> More than 50 years later, researchers at the City University of New York have made a version of this effect real — in a lab, without any actual black hole or physical spinning.
>
> The Breakthrough
> Instead of building a rotating object, the team created a ring-shaped network of resonators whose properties change over time in a carefully controlled way (spatiotemporal modulation). This synthetic “motion” mimics rotation through the Floquet effect, allowing them to observe superradiance — waves coming out with more energy than they went in.
>
> This is the first experimental confirmation of the Zel’dovich effect (an extension of Penrose’s idea) using purely electromagnetic waves in a non-rotating system.
>
> Why It Matters
> It bridges theoretical astrophysics with real-world photonics.
> The experiment opens doors to new types of ultra-efficient amplifiers and wave generators.
> It lets scientists study wave-matter interactions in rotating frames without needing massive, fast-spinning hardware.
>
> Previous experiments used spinning disks or cylinders, but this new approach eliminates mechanical rotation entirely — a cleaner, more elegant demonstration.
>
> While we’re still far from harvesting energy from real black holes, these tabletop analogs help us understand fundamental physics and could lead to revolutionary technologies in wave manipulation and energy harvesting.

### carlosfagar (@carlosfagar)
_Fri Jul 10 18:29:50 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 2 · ↻ 0 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/carlosfagar/status/2075648709300248993)

> $MRVL (Marvell Technology) es uno de los grandes beneficiarios silenciosos (y cada vez más ruidosos) del boom de la infraestructura de IA. Aquí te detallo los puntos clave que pediste de forma clara y actualizada (datos a julio 2026).
>
> 1. - La inversión de NVIDIA ($2.000 millones)
> El 31 de marzo de 2026, NVIDIA anunció una inversión de $2 mil millones en Marvell + una alianza estratégica profunda.
> Marvell se integra al ecosistema NVIDIA a través de NVLink Fusion, lo que permite que los custom XPUs (aceleradores de IA) y soluciones de networking de Marvell funcionen de forma nativa y compatible con la infraestructura de NVIDIA (incluyendo Vera CPU, ConnectX NICs, BlueField DPUs, NVLink y Spectrum-X switches).
> Además, colaborarán en silicon photonics y en llevar IA a redes de telecomunicaciones (AI-RAN para 5G/6G).
> ¿Por qué es tan importante?
> •  Valida a Marvell como proveedor de custom silicon de primer nivel.
> •  Da a los hyperscalers más flexibilidad: pueden usar GPUs NVIDIA + custom XPUs de Marvell en el mismo rack sin problemas de compatibilidad.
> •  Es una “co-opetición” inteligente: Marvell ayuda a escalar el ecosistema NVIDIA mientras compite en custom ASICs y óptica.
> El mercado reaccionó muy bien: MRVL subió fuerte ese día.

### carlosfagar (@carlosfagar)
_Fri Jul 10 18:30:02 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/carlosfagar/status/2075648758381990205)

> 2. Ventajas competitivas (el verdadero moat)
> Marvell tiene varias capas de ventaja:
> •  Liderazgo en óptica de alta velocidad: Es el referente mundial en PAM4 DSPs. Fue el primero en lanzar DSP de 1.6T en 5nm (Nova) y luego en 3nm (plataforma Ara). Sus productos Ara T, Ara X y Petra están ganando tracción masiva en 800G/1.6T para clusters de IA.
> •  Custom Silicon / XPUs de primer nivel: Junto con Broadcom, es de las únicas dos compañías capaces de diseñar y llevar a producción en volumen ASICs/XPUs extremadamente complejos (cientos de miles de millones de transistores). Trabaja con AWS (Trainium), Microsoft (Maia), Meta (MTIA) y Google. Ofrece un servicio end-to-end (arquitectura + IP + diseño + packaging avanzado + soporte de fabricación).
> •  Portfolio completo de data infrastructure: No solo hace una cosa. Tiene switches Ethernet de alto rendimiento (Teralynx hasta 51.2 Tbps), retimers PCIe 6 (Alaska P), CXL (Structera), Active Electrical Cables (AEC), Co-Packaged Optics (CPO) y silicon photonics. Es uno de los pocos que puede proveer casi todo el “nervio” de un data center de IA.
> •  IP y tecnología propietaria fuerte: Excelente portafolio de SerDes de ultra alta velocidad, analog/mixed-signal de bajo consumo y tecnologías de packaging avanzado (chiplets, CPO, HBM custom).
> •  Adquisición estratégica: Compró Celestial AI (óptica fotónica para scale-up interconnect), que potencia su posición en óptica de próxima generación.
> •  Altas barreras de entrada: Los design wins de custom silicon son multi-generacionales y crean switching costs muy altos. Una vez que un hyperscaler diseña su XPU con Marvell, es muy difícil y caro cambiar.

### carlosfagar (@carlosfagar)
_Fri Jul 10 18:30:03 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/carlosfagar/status/2075648763457085711)

> 3. ¿Qué productos hace realmente?
> Marvell se ha transformado en una compañía data infrastructure / AI-first. Sus productos principales hoy son:
> •  Custom AI accelerators (XPUs) y silicio adjunto (XPU-attach, NICs, CXL).
> •  Optical DSPs de alta velocidad (800G y 1.6T PAM4) → el motor de crecimiento actual.
> •  Switches Ethernet de data center (Teralynx family, hasta 51.2 Tbps, baja latencia).
> •  Interconnects de alta velocidad: Active Electrical Cables (AEC), PCIe retimers, CXL, silicon photonics y Co-Packaged Optics (CPO).
> •  Storage controllers (HDD y SSD) — sigue siendo un negocio sólido pero ya no es el principal driver.
> •  Otros (menor peso): DPUs, soluciones enterprise y carrier (5G).
> El Data Center ya representa ~75-76% de los ingresos y crece mucho más rápido que el resto.

Near-term it amps volatility across the whole photonics crew — a dip in AAOI becomes the perfect excuse for traders to hammer related plays like $LITE, $COHR, $FN, $AXTI, $CRDO, and even the smaller ones such as $POET or $ALMU. As the highest-beta name in the group, AAOI now functions like the ultimate risk-on/risk-off toggle for the sector. Watch those flows closely — the battlefield dynamics favor the prepared.

### favoritbookshop🚢 (@favoritbookshop)
_Fri Jul 10 18:52:39 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 2 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/favoritbookshop/status/2075654452158300439)

> AI's Next Bottleneck: Networking & Optics Could Become the Biggest Winners of the AI Infrastructure Cycle
> The AI investment narrative has largely centered on GPUs and compute. However, the next phase of the AI supercycle may be determined by an entirely different segment: networking and optical infrastructure.
> As AI clusters expand from thousands to millions of accelerators, moving data efficiently becomes just as important as generating compute power. Faster GPUs create little value if they spend time waiting for information to arrive.
> That is why the Networking & Optics Landscape deserves close attention.
> Current industry data highlights an unprecedented supply-demand imbalance:
> Coherent's Indium Phosphide (InP) lasers are reportedly sold out through 2027, supported by an exceptional 4x book-to-bill ratio.
> Ciena reached a record $7B order backlog, reflecting sustained demand from hyperscalers and telecom infrastructure.
> Lumentum expects approximately 77% revenue growth for FY2026, one of the strongest growth outlooks across semiconductor-adjacent industries.
> Unlike many AI segments where additional manufacturing capacity is gradually coming online, optical networking remains a genuine bottleneck. Every new AI data center requires high-speed optical interconnects, silicon photonics, switches, and advanced networking hardware before GPUs can operate at scale.
> The companies highlighted in this landscape represent nearly every critical layer of the ecosystem:
> Switching & Systems: Cisco, Arista, Ciena
> Interconnect Silicon: Marvell, Astera Labs, Credo, Macom
> Lasers & Optical Components: Coherent, Lumentum, Corning, Applied Optoelectronics
> Manufacturing: Fabrinet
> China Optics: Innolight, Eoptolink
> Silicon Photonics (Private): Lightmatter, Ayar Labs
> Crypto Investors Should Pay Attention
> Blockchain investors often focus on tokens directly tied to AI narratives, but the real capital cycle frequently begins with physical infrastructure.
> As hyperscalers continue deploying massive AI clusters, companies supplying networking hardware and optical components may capture significant value before downstream AI applications fully mature.
> The lesson for crypto markets is familiar: infrastructure tends to outperform during the early stages of transformational technology cycles. The same pattern previously benefited semiconductor manufacturers, cloud providers, and blockchain infrastructure projects.
> The AI race is no longer just about faster chips—it's increasingly about moving data at unprecedented speed. Until supply catches demand, networking and optics remain one of the strongest structural themes across the entire AI ecosystem.
> #AI #Crypto #Stocks #Tech

### My name is M. Only M (@musicandsoularg)
_Fri Jul 10 21:10:57 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 13 · ↻ 2 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/musicandsoularg/status/2075689255666352593)

> AVANCES EN TELEPORTACIÓN CUÁNTICA: EL CAMINO HACIA UN INTERNET ULTRASEGURO
>
> Investigadores de la Universidad de Ciencia y Tecnología de China han logrado un avance significativo en la teleportación cuántica a gran escala utilizando redes de fibra óptica de larga distancia, un paso crucial para el desarrollo de un internet cuántico prácticamente incorruptible.
>
> El experimento aprovecha el entrelazamiento cuántico, el fenómeno que Albert Einstein denominó "acción fantasmal a la distancia", donde el estado de dos partículas vinculadas se correlaciona sin importar la separación física entre ellas. Este sistema permite transferir estados cuánticos (información de la partícula) entre nodos distantes sin necesidad de desplazar la materia física en sí.
>
> Sin embargo, es importante aclarar un mito común en la física: este proceso no permite la comunicación instantánea ni supera la velocidad de la luz. Para que la teleportación cuántica se complete con éxito, los científicos siempre necesitan enviar datos adicionales a través de canales tradicionales (como cables de fibra óptica convencionales), lo que limita la velocidad final de la transmisión a los límites impuestos por la teoría de la relatividad.
>
> El verdadero hito de este avance no radica en la velocidad, sino en la seguridad y la fidelidad de la red. Al entrelazar las partículas, cualquier intento de interceptar, medir o espiar la información destruye de inmediato el estado cuántico, creando un ecosistema criptográfico inmune a los ciberataques y garantizando una privacidad digital absoluta para el futuro.
>
> Fuente: University of Science and Technology of China | Nature Photonics | MIT Technology Review

### P Equity Research 📰 (@pequityresearch)
_Fri Jul 10 21:27:22 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 203 · ↻ 43 · 💬 4 · [open on X](https://x.com/pequityresearch/status/2075693388158894328)

> Mirae Asset Securities: AI Bottleneck Issue
>
> Power Bottleneck
>
> > The Moment for Analog Semiconductors: The value of the analog domain, where Moore's Law does not apply, is exploding, giving suppliers overwhelming pricing power. Major players like TI, NXP, and Infineon are proving this dominant supplier market by executing synchronized price hikes in 2026.
>
> > The Physics of 12,500 Amperes and 800V DC: In ultra-high-density AI racks of 600kW to 1MW, sticking to traditional 48V power distribution causes the current to skyrocket to 12,500A, making operations impossible due to heat loss. Therefore, shifting the architecture to 800V to reduce the current to 750A and cut copper requirements by 45% is a physical inevitability.
>
> > Vertical Power Delivery (VPD): To prevent loss and voltage fluctuations during the "last inch" of stepping down to the GPU core voltage (around 0.7V), VPD—essentially the "CPO of the power world"—is emerging, which places the power converter directly beneath the GPU die.
>
> Signal & Photonics Bottleneck
>
> > Distance-Based Redistribution of Copper and Optics: The simplistic narrative that "optics will completely wipe out copper" is incorrect. A distance-based redistribution is intensifying, where copper and analog handle short distances (the scale-up domain) and optics take over long distances (rack-to-rack connectivity).
>
> > Semtech’s Analog Magic: In 200G/lane high-speed communication, Semtech's technology is garnering massive attention by completely eliminating DSPs (Digital Signal Processors)—which consume heavy power and cause latency—and correcting signals using only Analog Equalizers. This reduces power consumption by tenfold and slashes latency from nanoseconds (ns) to picoseconds (ps).
>
> > The Real Bottleneck in Optical Tech is the 'Light Source': While Co-Packaged Optics (CPO) is the correct long-term direction, the realistic winners for the next 2 to 3 years are Near-Packaged Optics (NPO) and 1.6T pluggable modules. The true bottlenecks in optical communication lie below the finished optical module layer: InP (Indium Phosphide) substrates, Continuous Wave (CW) laser sources, Photonics-SOI wafers (monopolized by Soitec), and SiPho foundries.
>
> > Network Reliability and 'Link Flap': The "Link Flap" phenomenon, where an optical link momentarily blinks, disrupts the synchronization (all-reduce) of the entire AI cluster and leaves GPUs idling. In massive clusters, solutions that guarantee reliability rather than just bandwidth (such as Credo's Zero-Flap) become the ultimate bottleneck determining economic viability.
>
> $TSEM $COHR $LITE $AAOI $MRVL $LITE $TSM $INTC $GFS $FN $SMTC $MTSI $APH $CRDO

> AI Bottlenecks Explained:
>
> Key Current Bottlenecks
> •Power/Energy — Primary constraint: Massive electricity demand for compute + cooling; grid delays, transformers, and generation shortages.
>
>         •Memory (HBM) — High-bandwidth memory supply sold out; critical for GPU performance.
>
>          •Networking/Interconnects — Data movement between GPUs (optical, switches, photonics) causing bottlenecks.
>
>          •Cooling & Power Delivery — Liquid cooling and electrical systems strained by high-density AI racks.
>

>
> Power/Energy (hottest area):
> •Vertiv $VRT — Cooling & power management.

### P Equity Research 📰 (@pequityresearch)
_Fri Jul 10 23:40:32 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 293 · ↻ 35 · 💬 13 · [open on X](https://x.com/pequityresearch/status/2075726900291416365)

> Rosenblatt: Optical
>
> Context Behind Recent Sector Weakness
>
> > China InP Capacity Scare: Stocks traded poorly over the last 1–2 months due to fears that expanding indium phosphide (InP) capacity in China could crash laser pricing.
>
> > CPO Timing Rumors: Reports suggested a potential one-year delay for large-scale Co-Packaged Optics (CPO) deployment compared to the base expectation of a 2H27 build and 2028 shipment.
>
> > Short Seller Dynamics: Checks indicate short sellers are exploiting this mid-quarter noise without genuine conviction. Many plan to cover their positions before 2QCY26 earnings roll out in late July/early August and intend to go long on Optical stocks by 2027 to capture the 2028–2030 CPO ramp.
>
> Assessing the China InP Threat
>
> > Supply vs. Demand: Chinese players could add 20% to 40% to Rosenblatt's 2030 non-China InP laser capacity forecast of ~$26bn. However, total 2030 InP capacity is still projected to fall 40% behind aggregate demand, mitigating oversupply risks.
>
> > Technological Moat: Near-term Western pricing remains secure because Chinese manufacturers currently lack 200G EMLs and high-power CW (continuous wave) lasers required for CPO and Near-Packaged Optics (NPO) applications. They currently possess low-power CWs for SiPo transceivers and 100G EMLs for 800G transceivers.
>
> > Market Decoupling: Long-term Western and Chinese supply chain dynamics are unlikely to be fungible due to political decoupling and the technical shift toward CPO. Western leaders like Lumentum (LITE) and Coherent (COHR) are already fully sold out through 2027 and into 2028, bolstered by major pre-buys from companies like NVIDIA.
>
> Dongshan Precision: Recently greenlit a $1.2bn expansion in Changzhou for InP lasers and 1.6T transceivers after acquiring Source Photonics.
>
> Sanan IC: Pivoting from LEDs to InP, expanding capacity from 2,750 to 6,000 6-inch wafers per month.
>
> HiSense Optoelectronics & Accelink: Also actively growing InP capacity
>
> Architecture & Structural Industry Demands
>
> > CPO Timeline Intact: The smaller-scale CPO timeline (2H26 build, 2027 ship) remains on track, with 2027 production estimates ranging from 30K to over 350K units each for NVIDIA and Broadcom. 2028 remains the definitive volume inflection year for large-scale CPO, with NPO filling the intermediate gap in 2027.
>
> > Network Flattening Already Priced In: Concerns that technologies like Multipath Reliable Connection (MRC) and Resilient Network Graphs (RNG) will hurt demand are overblown. While larger radix Ethernet switches reduce transceivers per switch from 6–7 down to 3–4, exponential XPU volume growth easily offsets the lower ratio.
>
> > Alternative Laser Architectures (GaAs / VCSELs): 200G VCSELs (made from Gallium Arsenide rather than InP) are emerging as intermediate NPO solutions. Broadcom is looking at them for 3.2T NPO platforms, while Lumentum and startup PicoJool have demonstrated VCSEL-based solutions to circumvent potential InP supply constraints in GPU-to-GPU interconnects.
>
> Key Company Earnings Setups
>
> > Lumentum ($LITE): Toughest near-term setup because it has provided the most forward guidance, though it remains highly attractive at ~$700. Investors are watching if it can accelerate its CY27 target of $2bn in quarterly revenue with 40+% operating margins.
>
> > Coherent ($COHR): Highly favored due to accelerating internal 200G EML/CW laser production and a major new ~$1bn/year 1.6T transceiver contract win with Google (sourcing Mitsubishi lasers). Long-term margins will be supported by 11-figure LTAs with NVIDIA for 2027–2030.
>
> > Applied Optoelectronics ($AAOI): Expected to deliver a "beat and raise" watershed 2Q26. Driven by 800G sales to Amazon and Oracle, revenues are expected to exceed $200mn in 2Q26, with 3Q26 guidance pointing to ~$300mn and gross margin expansion well north of the ~30% level seen in 1H26.
>
> > Arista Networks ($ANET): Positioned for strong growth via massive deployment wins with Meta, Microsoft, Oracle, OpenAI/Anthropic, and Google (which could become a 10% customer in 2026). High deferred revenue recognition is expected to fuel >30% revenue growth in 2H26 and 40+% in 2027.
>
> > Fabrinet ($FN): Positioned for solid sequential Datacom growth with NVIDIA alongside initial revenue contributions from new Datacom customers Amazon and Lumentum.
>
> > Viavi Solutions ($VIAV): Safe from InP noise as it has no direct exposure. Growth is driven by testing systems (transceiver/OCS) and MilAero products, with CPO/NPO testing revenues slated to begin this fall.
>
> > Ciena ($CIEN): Ciena's order book suggest that Data Center Interconnect (DCI) and scale-out orders are poised to reaccelerate from previous levels.

### john jacket (@jacket82488)
_Sat Jul 11 14:32:21 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/jacket82488/status/2075951330305474659)

> 【半導体・AIインフラの地殻変動】 「AIの限界はソフトではなく物理（電力と信号）にある」
> 現在、AIクラスターが直面している「電力」と「光・信号」の圧倒的な物理的ボトルネック、そしてその裏で覇権を握る黒幕企業について、Techトレンドをまとめました。
>
> 半導体投資やインフラに関わる人は【ブックマーク】推奨です🧵👇
>
> ⚡ 電力のボトルネック：アナログの逆襲と物理の限界
>
> アナログ半導体の時代到来：ムーアの法則が適用されないアナログ領域の価値が爆発中。TI、NXP、Infineon等の主要ベンダーは2026年に一斉値上げを断行。供給側が圧倒的な価格決定権を持つ市場へシフトしている。
> 12,500Aと800V直流の物理的限界：600kW〜1MW級の超高密度AIラックで従来の48V給電を続けると、電流は12,500Aに激増し熱損失で崩壊する。電流を750Aに抑え、銅材を45%削減できる「800V架構」への移行は物理的な必然。
>
> VPD（垂直電力給電）：GPUコア（約0.7V）への降圧時の損失を防ぐため、電源変換器をGPUチップの「真下」に配置するVPD（電源界のCPO）が急速に台頭。
> 📡 信号・光学のボトルネック：銅の延命と光の現実
>
> 「光が銅を完全駆逐」は誤り：実際は距離に応じた住み分け。短距離（Scale-up領域）は銅線とアナログコンポーネントが粘り、長距離（ラック間接続）を光が担う。
> Semtechのアナログ・マジック：200G/laneの超高速通信において、消費電力と遅延の元凶であるDSPを完全に排除し、アナログイコライザのみで信号を補正するSemtechの技術が激アツ。消費電力を10分の1に、遅延をns（ナノ秒）からps（ピコ秒）へと一気に縮小。
>
> 真のボトルネックは「光源」にあり：長期的な正解はCPOだが、今後2〜3年の現実的な勝者はNPOや1.6T可挿入型モジュール。本当のボトルネックはさらに下流の、InP（インジウムリン）基板、CWレーザー光源、Soitecが独占するPhotonics-SOIウェハ、そしてシリコンフォトニクス（SiPho）ファウンドリにある。
> 網 ネットワーク信頼性と「Link Flap」の恐怖
>
> Link Flap現象がすべてを止める：光リンクが一瞬だけ瞬断する「Link Flap」が発生すると、AIクラスター全体の同期演算（all-reduce）が中断され、膨大なGPUが完全なアイドル状態（サボり）になる。
> 帯域よりも信頼性の時代へ：超巨大クラスターにおいて、単に帯域を広げるだけでなく、この瞬断を絶対に起こさない信頼性を保証できるソリューション（Credoの『Zero-Flap』など）が、AIビジネスの経済性を左右する最終ボトルネックになっている。
>
> 💡 まとめAIの進化は、最先端の1nm/2nmプロセスだけでなく、それを支える「電源（VPD/800V）」や「アナログ信号処理（Semtech等）」、「光源のサプライチェーン（Soitec等）」にいかに強みを持つかで勝負が決まるフェーズに入っています。
> #生成AI #半導体 #NVDA #株クラ #テクノロジー

**Media**
- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HM9CujybEAAYGTJ.jpg

### TickerTalks (@TickerTalksX)
_Sat Jul 11 15:31:00 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/TickerTalksX/status/2075966091910877371)

> Before a chip ships, it gets "burned in": baked under heat and voltage for hours so the ones destined to fail early die on the test bench, not in the field.
>
> $AEHR (Aehr Test Systems) builds the machines that do this at the wafer level. It grew up testing the silicon carbide chips in EVs.
>
> On July 9 its lead silicon photonics customer placed a follow-on production order for those systems, to burn in the optical transceivers that shuttle data between chips inside AI data centers.
>
> Same testing step, now moving from EV power into the optical layer of the AI buildout. The stock has more than tripled in the past year. Fiscal Q4 numbers land July 14.

### ᜱ𐤠㇜I ⵉ ᜤ 👽 ᜱ । ⚡︎ । ⚛ ᜤ (@ValienVision)
_Sat Jul 11 16:11:28 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/ValienVision/status/2075976273768137041)

> Physical AI pick-and-shovel ⌁ $NOVT DD  🔖🛸
>
> I spend a loooot of time evaluating the physical AI stack... with perhaps a slightly greater focus on humanoids.
>
> Software models are expanding at an extraordinary pace, yet the immediate scaling constraint remains entirely hardware-bound.
>
> Advanced whole-body control policies require instant, flawless translation into the physical world. 
> It starts with perception, flows through planning and control, then reaches the physical world through motion, force feedback and actuation.
>
> Every stage compounds error, so micro-second precision and adaptive force feedback determine whether an AI brain can function in reality or fail during contact-rich tasks.
>
> The sim2real gap is a hardware execution problem... 
>
> That's why I keep coming back to Novanta.
>
> The company has built an ecosystem that occupies the exact center of this hardware constraint. 
> They deliberately focus on manufacturing the core precision motion, sensing, and also photonics stacks that advanced robotics OEMs require.
>
> 🛸 ⌁ Motion stack
> Precision motion from Celera Motion and Ingenia supplies the encoders (Aura series and IncOder CORE), frameless and slotless high-torque motors (Omni+ line), and certified servo drives (Denali and Everest Safe equipped with FSoE).
>
> The result is (custom) actuators with sub-micron feedback and cogging-free smoothness paired with deterministic real-time control loops needed for stable locomotion and fluid multi-DOF manipulation. 
>
> 🛸 ⌁ Sensing stack
> ATI Industrial Automation (one of their greatest acquisition) contributes multi-axis force/torque sensors from the Axia and Varo families together with automatic tool changers and material removal tools that turn position-controlled arms into systems capable of compliant grasping, adaptive manipulation, and importantly safe human interaction. 
>
> These components matter for collision detection in unstructured environments and for force-modulated actions where pure kinematic control falls short.
>
> 🛸 ⌁ Photonics stack
> The photonics capabilities, built around Cambridge Technology beam steering, Synrad CO2 sources, Laser Quantum solid-state and ultrafast lasers, plus ARGES scanning, support high-precision material processing. 
>
> That matters both for manufacturing the next generation of robots and for the AI-optimized production cells those robots will eventually run inside factories and warehouses.
>
> The laser sources, beam steering, scan heads, and related photonics technologies supplied by Novanta are also used in medical laser procedures, such as ophthalmology, dermatology/plastic surgery, soft tissue applications, and support for minimally invasive/robotic surgery systems.
>
> 🛸 ⌁ Healthcare stack (robotics surgery)
> Continuing on the medical side, WOM insufflators, NDS visualization systems, but also integrated motion solutions underpin minimally invasive and robotic procedures. 
>
> Riverpoint brings high-growth minimally invasive surgical consumables (like advanced surgical fibers, sutures, and implants for trauma and cardiovascular applications).
>
> As AI moves into semi-autonomous subtasks in surgery to autonomous surgery, the same precision motion and force sensing that serve humanoids translate directly into safer, more consistent tissue interaction and better visualization pipelines, and vice-versa. 
>
> 🛸 ⌁ Final thoughts
> What stands out is how the pieces fit together.
>
> Acquisitions stitched a full motion and sensing stack, with end-effector tooling and supporting photonics into one offering. 
>
> That integration reduces risk for OEMs who must hit safety and reliability thresholds for real-world deployments. 
>
> Physical AI patform builders still do the system integration and higher-level control. Novanta supplies the subsystems that let those platforms actually perform at the edge of what physics allows.
>
> $NOVT

### Funniest lines (@funniestlines)

### Yunis Rzayev (@rzayev7895)
_Sat Jul 11 18:38:31 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 60 · ↻ 0 · 💬 5 · [open on X](https://x.com/rzayev7895/status/2076013282071306423)

> KULICKE & SOFFA INDUSTRIES, INC. ( $KLIC)
>
> Kapsamlı Şirket Değerleme ve Stratejik Analiz 
>
> 1. Yönetici Özeti ve Stratejik Yol Ayrımı
>
> Yarı iletken endüstrisinde Moore Kanunu'nun fiziksel sınırlara dayanması ve ön uç (front-end) litografi maliyetlerinin katlanarak artması, performans artışının yeni odağını İleri Seviye Paketleme  ve Heterojen Entegrrasyon süreçlerine kaydırmıştır. Kulicke & Soffa, tarihsel olarak otomotiv, endüstriyel ve tüketici elektroniğine hitap eden olgun tel bağlama pazarında %80’e yakın pazar payıyla ezici bir cash cow yönetmektedir. Ancak şirket, son iki yıldır akademik ve kurumsal analizlere konu olan (örneğin 2025 sonundaki Harvard Business School stratejik vaka analizindeki gibi) çok kritik bir yol ayrımındadır: Olgun pazarlardaki nakit akışını koruyarak, yapay zeka (AI) ve yüksek performanslı bilgi işlem (HPC) çiplerinin mimarisini belirleyen ileri seviye montaj teknolojilerine liderlik etmek.
>
> FY2026 ikinci çeyrek sonuçları ve güncel pazar dinamikleri, KLIC’in bu teknolojik dönüşümü başarıyla gerçekleştirdiğini ve döngüsel bir dipten çıkış (cyclical inflection) dönemine girdiğini doğrulamaktadır. Şirket, karlılığı düşük olan Electronics Assembly iş kolunu tamamen kapatarak odağını netleştirmiş, yapay zeka veri merkezlerindeki bant genişliği kısıtlamalarını çözen Thermo-Compression Bonding ve Silicon Photonics çözümlerinde vites artırmıştır.
>
> 2. Finansal Performans ve Döngüsel Kaldıraç Analizi
>
> KLIC’in finansal yapısı, arka uç (back-end) sermaye ekipmanı üreticilerinde görülen yüksek operasyonel kaldıraç karakteristiğini taşımaktadır. Sektörel envanter düzeltmelerinin sona ermesiyle birlikte, gelir artışı marjlar üzerinde çarpan etkisi yaratmaktadır.
>
> Çeyreklik Finansal Gerçekleşmeler ve Dinamikler
>
> -- Gelir İvmesi: Q2 FY2026 net geliri, bir önceki çeyreğe göre %21.5, geçen yılın aynı dönemine göre ise %49.8 artarak 242.6 milyon USD seviyesine ulaşmıştır. Bu rakam, konsensüs beklentisi olan 191.4 milyon USD’yi büyük bir sürprizle geride bırakmıştır.
>
> -- Brüt Kar Marjı Genişlemesi: Brüt marj %49.3 olarak gerçekleşmiştir. Geçen yılın aynı çeyreğindeki %24.9'luk seviyeye kıyasla 2,440 baz puanlık operasyonel genişleme, yüksek marjlı Advanced Solutions ve bellek ürün miksinin devreye girmesiyle açıklanmaktadır.
>
> -- Karlılığa Dönüş: GAAP operasyonel karı 38.5 milyon USD'ye yükselmiştir. Geçen yılın aynı döneminde kaydedilen ağır zararların ardından, Non-GAAP operasyonel kar marjı %19.1’e (46.3 milyon USD) fırlamıştır. Non-GAAP EPS ise 0.79 USD ile beklentilerin 0.12 USD üzerinde gelmiştir.
>
> Q3 ve Q4 FY2026 Öngörüleri
>
> Şirketin resmi Q3 FY2026 kılavuzu, ardışık olarak %28 büyüme ile 310 milyon USD gelir hedeflemektedir. Operasyonel giderlerin (OpEx) 85 milyon USD seviyesine çıkması, üretim hacmini (production ramp) desteklemek için yapılan mühendislik istihdamları ve değişken performans primlerinden kaynaklanmaktadır. Yönetim, Q4 FY2026 döneminde de Q3'e kıyasla %5 ile %10 arasında organik bir büyüme trendinin korunacağını öngörmektedir. Bu doğrultuda FY2026 toplam geliri yaklaşık 1.07 milyar USD bandına doğru ilerlemektedir.
>
> 3. Segment Bazında Operasyonel ve Teknolojik Derinleşme
>
> KLIC’in ürün portföyü, yarı iletken dünyasının hem olgun hem de en uç teknolojilerine eş zamanlı hizmet verecek şekilde yeniden yapılandırılmıştır.
>
> -- Olgun Pazarlar: Ball/Wedge Bonding ──> Nakit Üretimi & Hacim (Akıllı Telefon, Otomotiv, Endüstriyel)
>
> -- Seküler Pazarlar: Advanced Solutions ──> TCB, FTC, ProMEM Suite, Vertical Wire (AI, HPC, HBM)
>
> -- İstikrar Segmenti: APS ──> Fabrika Kullanım Oranlarına Bağlı Yedek Parça ve Servis Güvencesi
>
> A. Geleneksel ve Hafif Döngüsel Segmentler
>
> -- Ball Bonding Equipment (Tarihsel Pay: %44.8): Klasik altın ve bakır tel bağlama sistemleridir. Akıllı telefon, PC ve alt segment tüketici elektroniğindeki döngüsel toparlanma, bu segmenti Q2 FY2026'da yeniden ana gelir sürücülerinden biri haline getirmiştir (GenSemi gelirleri çeyreklik %19.4 artışla 148.9 milyon USD olmuştur).
>
> -- Wedge Bonding Equipment (Tarihsel Pay: %16.9): Güç yarı iletkenleri, elektrikli araç (EV) batarya paketleri ve endüstriyel modüllere hizmet eder. Otomotiv sektöründeki elektrifikasyon trendiyle daha stabil bir grafik çizmektedir.
>
> -- Aftermarket Products & Services (APS) (Tarihsel Pay: %23.9): Küresel kurulu makine parkının sarf malzemeleri ve servis hizmetleridir. Donanım satışları düşse dahi, fabrikaların çalışmasına paralel olarak sürekli nakit üreten, döngüselliği en düşük defansif kalkandır.
>
> B. Yeni Nesil Hafıza (Memory) ve Güç Çözümleri (2026 İnovasyonları)
>
> Bellek segmenti, kurumsal SSD (eSSD) ve yüksek performanslı sunucu talebiyle Q2 FY2026'da çeyreklik bazda %93 büyüme kaydederek 31.3 milyon USD'ye ulaşmıştır. Şirket bu ivmeyi kalıcı kılmak adına Mart 2026'da iki büyük teknolojik silahını duyurmuştur:
>
> 1. ProMEM Suite: Standart yüksek hacimli bellek montajında (Stacked NAND) üretkenliği ve proses kontrolünü dramatik şekilde artıran bir ball bonding yazılım ve donanım paketidir.
>
> 2. Vertical Wire Teknolojisi (ATP MEM PLUS): Geleneksel tel bağlamayı dikey boyuta taşıyarak ara bağlantı yoğunluğunu artırır ve paket ayak izini küçültür. Stacked DRAM ve yeni nesil yüksek yoğunluklu bellek mimarilerinde silikon delikli geçişlere (TSV) karşı son derece maliyet etkin bir alternatif sunmaktadır.
>
> 4. Gelişmiş Paketleme ve AI Altyapı Katalizörü
>
> Advanced Solutions segmenti altındaki Thermo-Compression Bonding (TCB), KLIC'in uzun vadeli seküler büyüme motorudur. Şirket, TCB iş kolunun FY2026’da çeyreklik bazda en az %70 büyüyeceğini ve tek başına 100 milyon USD+ barajını aşacağını doğrulamıştır.
>
> Fluxless TCB (FTC) ve Teknik Üstünlük
>
> Gelişmiş veri merkezi işlemcilerinde kullanılan alt bileşenlerin kalınlıkları azaldıkça ve kalıp boyutları büyüdükçe (30 mm ve üzeri), geleneksel "flip-chip" yöntemleri termal eğrilme ve hizalama hatalarına neden olmaktadır. KLIC’in Fluxless TCB (FTC) teknolojisi bu problemi şu inovasyonlarla çözmektedir:
>
> -- Mikron Altı Hassasiyet: Lehim tabanlı bağlantıları 10 μm hatveye (pitch), doğrudan bakır-bakır bağlantıları ise en az 5 μm hatveye kadar indirebilmektedir.
>
> -- Formik Asit Buharı Oksit İndirgeme: Süreç esnasında sıvı akı (flux) kullanılmadığı için kalıplar arasında neredeyse "sıfır boşluk yüksekliği" elde edilir; bu da elektriksel direnci düşürür ve termal yönetimi optimize eder.
>
> -- Co-Packaged Optics ve Silikon Fotonik: Yapay zeka kümelerindeki anahtarlama ve ağ hızlarını artırmak için optik transceiver bileşenlerinin doğrudan işlemci yanına TCB ile montajlanması sürecinde KLIC, küresel lider dökümhanelerden ve OSAT'lardan peş peşe siparişler almaktadır.
>
> 5. Kapasite Genişletme ve Gelecek Projeksiyonları
>
> Advanced Solutions segmentinin ölçeklenebilmesi için üretim darboğazlarının aşılması gerekmektedir. Şirket yönetimi bu doğrultuda stratejik bir sermaye hamlesi yapmıştır:
>
> 1. CapEx Artırımı
> CapEx Artırımı:FY2026 Dönemi.Şirket, yıllık sermaye harcaması (CapEx) bütçesini 12 milyon USD seviyesinden 22 milyon USD seviyesine neredeyse iki katına çıkarmıştır.
>
> 2. Üretim Hatlarının Modernizasyonu:
> Q3/Q4 FY2026. Artırılan bütçe doğrudan Singapur ve ilgili üretim tesislerinde Fluxless TCB ve dikey tel montaj hatlarının otomasyon kalitesini yükseltmek için kullanılmaktadır.
>
> 3.Kapasite Hedefine Ulaşılması:
> Erken FY2027. Yapılan bu yatırımlarla Advanced Solutions segmentinin yıllık üretim ve sevkiyat kapasitesi run-rate bazında 400 milyon USD satış potansiyeline ulaştırılacaktır.
>
> Sipariş birikimini gösteren backlog yapısı da bu süreci desteklemektedir ve hızla artmakdadır. Siparişlerin iptal edilebilir olması bir risk olsa da Çin, Tayvan ve Kore'deki fabrika kullanım oranlarının %90'ın üzerinde seyretmesi, bu siparişlerin büyük ölçüde realizasyonla sonuçlanacağını göstermektedir.
>
> 6. Sektörel Karşılaştırma ve İleri Dönük Değerleme Modeli
>
> Yarı iletken ekipman pazarında değerleme yapılırken ön uç (ASML, KLA, Lam Research, Applied Materials) ve arka uç (KLIC, Besi, ASMPT) ayrımı kritik rol oynar. Ön uç firmaları daha az döngüsel ve yüksek bariyerli oldukları için tarihsel olarak yüksek çarpanlara sahiptir.
>
> KLIC ise tarihsel olarak olgun wire bonder pazarının dalgalanmalarına maruz kaldığı için düşük çarpanla işlem görmüştür. Fakat Advanced Solutions segmentinin kapasitesinin 400 milyon USD'ye ayarlanması ve TCB'nin yüksek karlılığı, çarpan genişlemesini tetiklemektedir.
>
> Akran Grubu Karşılaştırma Analizi (FOTO - 1)
>
> 2027 Gelir ve Çarpan Projeksiyonu
>
> -- FY2026 Tahmini Gelir: ~1.07 milyar USD (Mevcut çeyreklik gidişat ve Q3 kılavuzu tabanlı).
>
> -- FY2027 Projeksiyon Geliri: Bellek toparlanması, ProMEM Suite adaptasyonu ve TCB'nin yıllık 100 milyon USD'lik barajı kırıp Advanced Solutions run-rate'ini yukarı taşımasıyla 1.25 milyar USD (%17-20 civarı bir yıllık büyüme).
>
> -- Değerleme Yaklaşımı: Advanced Packaging payının artması sebebiyle şirkete hak ettiği tarihsel iskontonun üzerinde, 6x Forward P/S (İleri Dönük Satış) çarpanı uygulanması rasyoneldir. Bu çarpan altında şirketin adil kurumsal değeri 7.5 milyar USD olarak hesaplanmaktadır.
>
> Şirketin kasasındaki 254.3 milyon USD net nakit ve sıfır borç yapısı, hisse başına değer hesaplamasında ekstra bir emniyet marjı sunmaktadır. Finansal modelleme kapsamında %8 iskonto oranı tatbik edildiğinde, hisse senedinin önümüzdeki 12 aylık periyotta 135 USD adil değer hedefine doğru re-rate edilmesi beklenmektedir. Bu da mevcut konsolide fiyata göre yaklaşık %20 yukarı potansiyel anlamına gelir.
>
> 7. Derinlemesine Risk ve Tehdit Analizi
>
> Risk Matrisi ve Stratejik Tehditler: KLIC pozisyonlanmasında aşağı yönlü risklerin yakından izlenmesi gerekmektedir.
>
> I. İkame Teknolojiler ve Hibrit Bağlama Tehdidi
>
> En uç seviye AI hızlandırıcılarında (NVIDIA, AMD vb. yeni nesil mimarileri) TCB hatvelerinin dahi yetersiz kaldığı noktalarda Hybrid Bonding (Doğrudan Bakır-Bakır Die-to-Wafer entegrasyonu) devreye girmektedir. Bu alanda Hollandalı BE Semiconductor (Besi) tartışmasız pazar lideridir ve ana dökümhanelerin (TSMC vb.) onaylı tedarikçisidir.
>
> Risk: Eğer Hybrid Bonding teknolojisi beklenenden daha hızlı ucuzlar ve orta segment çiplere de hızla adapte edilirse, KLIC'in TCB pazarı daralabilir. KLIC, 2024'ten bu yana kendi bünyesindeki Hibrit Bağlama AR-GE programını hızlandırdığını ve erken müşteri test aşamasında olduğunu (Mart 2026 güncellemelerinde) belirtse de Besi ile olan teknolojik ve zamansal makası kapatamama riski mevcuttur.
>
> II. Müşteri Konsantrasyonu ve Kamçı Etkisi
> KLIC’in gelir yapısı son derece dikeydir. En büyük 10 müşteri (büyük OSAT'lar olan ASE, Amkor ve dev IDM'ler) toplam grup gelirlerinin %55'ini oluşturmaktadır.
>
> Risk: Son tüketici elektroniğindeki ani bir makroekonomik durgunluk, bu 10 dev firmanın CapEx bütçelerini anında dondurmasına yol açar. Arka uç üreticileri, tedarik zincirinin en sonunda yer aldığından "Kamçı Etkisi" nedeniyle sipariş iptallerini veya ertelemelerini en şiddetli hisseden grup olmaktadır.
>
> III. Jeopolitik Sıkışma ve Doğu Asya Riski
>
> KLIC her ne kadar Singapur merkezli ve ABD operasyonlu bir yapıya sahip olsa da en büyük yarı iletken montaj müşterileri ve dökümhaneleri Tayvan, Çin Halk Cumhuriyeti ve Güney Kore sınırları içerisindedir.
>
> Risk: ABD-Çin ticaret savaşlarının gelişmiş paketleme ekipmanlarına (özellikle TCB ve alt bileşenlerine) yönelik getirebileceği ek ihracat yasakları veya Tayvan Boğazı'ndaki olası bir lojistik aksama, şirketin backlog teslimatlarını tamamen felç edebilir.
>
> IV. CapEx ve Marj Baskısı
>
> Yıllık CapEx'in 12 milyon USD'den 22 milyon USD'ye çıkarılması, kısa vadede nakit akışını ve serbest nakit akışı marjlarını (Q2 FY2026'da düzeltilmiş serbest nakit akışı 6.3 milyon USD seviyesindedir) baskılamaktadır. Yeni hatların verimlilik oranlarında yaşanabilecek herhangi bir operasyonel aksaklık, Q3 ve Q4 brüt marj tahminlerini aşağı yönlü revize ettirebilir.
>
> 8. Stratejik Sonuç
>
> Kulicke & Soffa, döngüsel bir çöküşün ardından operasyonel karlılığa dönüş hikayesini başarıyla yazmıştır. Şirket, geleneksel iş kollarının sağladığı güçlü nakit akışını, geleceğin AI ve bellek standartları olan TCB, ProMEM ve dikey tel teknolojilerine başarıyla aktarmaktadır. Hisse senedinde son aylarda yaşanan güçlü momentum ve ralli, bu döngüsel dönüşün pazar tarafından satın alınmaya başladığını gösterse de FY2027 projeksiyonlarımız doğrultusunda şirketin çarpan büyümesinin henüz tamamlanmadığı değerlendirilmektedir. Bilançosunda borç bulunmayan, düzenli çeyreklik temettü ödeyen ve hisse geri alımlarıyla paydaş değerini destekleyen KLIC, uzun vadeli yarı iletken portföylerinde temel bir arka uç pozisyonu olarak öne çıkmaktadır.
>
> Yatırım tavsiyesi değildir.

- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HM97DT7awAADfHC.png

### Kantique (@KantiqueTech)
_Sat Jul 11 19:03:01 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 13 · ↻ 4 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/KantiqueTech/status/2076019446376775983)

> 🚨Pendant la ruée vers l’or quantique, qui vend les pioches ?
>
> Si le calcul quantique explose, ce ne sont pas forcément les constructeurs de processeurs qui captureront toute la valeur. 
>
> Comme au XIXe siècle, les vrais gagnants pourraient être ceux qui fournissent les outils indispensables à tous.
>
> Les fournisseurs de l’ombre :
>
> •  Cryogénie : Oxford Instruments, Bluefors et Leiden Cryogenics dominent les réfrigérateurs à dilution qui refroidissent les systèmes supraconducteurs à quelques millikelvins. 
>
> Un goulot d’étranglement critique que personne ne peut contourner facilement.
>
> •  Lasers et photonique : TOPTICA       Photonics, M Squared Lasers, Coherent ($COHR ), Lumentum ($LITE ) et IPG Photonics fournissent les systèmes de précision nécessaires aux ions piégés et atomes neutres.
>
> •  Électronique de contrôle : FormFactor ($FORM ) et ses stations de test cryogéniques, ou MKS Instruments ($MKSI ), sont indispensables pour caractériser et faire fonctionner les puces quantiques.
>
> Ces entreprises vendent à toutes les modalités (supraconducteur, ion piégé, photonique, atome neutre). 
>
> Peu importe qui gagne la course aux qubits, elles restent essentielles.
>
> Dans la révolution quantique, les pioches et les pelles pourraient bien rapporter plus sûrement que l’or lui-même.
>
> Kantique — Le quantique décrypté.

### Melvin (@MelvinInvests)
_Sat Jul 11 19:35:17 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 79 · ↻ 26 · 💬 6 · [open on X](https://x.com/MelvinInvests/status/2076027568684401094)

> This is the supply chain that is running the entire AI revolution and here is how you can benefit from it (Save this). 
>
> When NVIDIA builds a GPU, the chip itself is only part of the story and those GPUs need to talk to each other at extraordinary speeds, across the same rack, across racks, across entire data centers. 
>
> The question of how data moves between chips is the defining bottleneck of the AI era and the answer is silicon photonics, moving data using light instead of copper wire.
>
> Think of copper as a country road and silicon photonics as a superhighway. 
>
> As AI clusters scale from one rack to hundreds of racks running millions of calculations simultaneously, copper runs out of bandwidth while light does not and here is you can benefit from this.
>
> Coherent ($COHR ) is the dominant supplier of optical transceivers and lasers inside every high-speed AI rack.  
>
> Their Q3 FY2026 revenue hit $1.81 billion, up 21% year over year with datacenter and communications now making up 72% of total revenue.  
>
> They are doubling their indium phosphide wafer capacity by end of year, a manufacturing advantage that produces four times the chips at less than half the cost of older technology.
>
> Marvell ($MRVL) spans both the copper switching layer and the silicon photonics layer through its Celestial AI acquisition, making it the most complete play across the entire networking stack.
>
> Corning ($GLW) is the fiber and every photon traveling between racks and between data centers travels through Corning's glass and they are expanding US fiber production by more than 50% and building three new manufacturing plants.
>
> Fabrinet ($FN) is the contract manufacturer that physically builds the optical modules for Coherent, Lumentum, and others.  
>
> Every time an optical company wins a new NVIDIA contract, Fabrinet's production volume goes up and it is a pure leverage on the entire sector without having to pick a winner between the component makers.
>
> IntelliEPI appears in both the SOI wafer layer and the light source layer of this supply chain, making them a double exposure name across two critical inputs.  
>
> When photonics capacity doubles, EPI wafer demand doubles first and almost no one tracks wafer substrate suppliers at this level.
>
> The thesis is simple as AI demand requires exponentially more data movement between chips, copper cannot keep up and light is the only solution. 
>
> Make sure to follow me @MelvinInvests for more overlooked opportunities in AI infrastructure.

- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HM-GfHmXoAAD9sN.jpg

### Art of Speculation (@ArtofSpecuycky)
_Sat Jul 11 20:14:57 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 218 · ↻ 49 · 💬 30 · [open on X](https://x.com/ArtofSpecuycky/status/2076037548632363499)

> 光通信板块为什么跌这么惨？拆解Rosenblatt最新报告，聊聊我自己的判断
>
> 市场的担忧从哪来？
> 主要是三个因素叠加在一起：
> 一是市场担心中国厂商正在快速扩产磷化铟(InP)激光器产能， 害怕未来供给暴增导致价格战。
> 二是市场传出CPO(共封装光学)可能要推迟大约一年才能大规模部署， 这让不少人开始怀疑未来几年的光通信需求会不会跟着延后。
> 三是不少空头其实并不是真的看空这条赛道的基本面， 只是在借着这些消息和财报前的空窗期制造恐慌， 甚至有相当一部分空头计划在7月底、8月初财报公布前陆续回补空单， 部分人还打算2027年重新做多整个板块， 提前布局2028到2030年的CPO超级周期。
>
> 中国扩产到底是不是真正的威胁？
> 这是市场最关心的问题， 但我认为担心得有点过头了。 第一， 即便中国厂商持续扩产， 预计到2030年全球InP激光器的供给相比需求仍然存在大约40%的缺口， 行业整体依然缺货， 扩产短期内不会导致供给过剩。 
> 第二， 中国目前主要能量产的是低功率连续波激光器和100G EML， 应用场景集中在硅光收发器和800G模块这些相对成熟的产品线， 但真正未来几年最赚钱的200G EML和高功率连续波激光器， 中国还没有成熟的量产能力， 而这两样恰恰是CPO和NPO最核心的光源器件， 这意味着未来几年欧美厂商在高端环节依然握有明显的技术优势。 
> 第三， 中美供应链本身也在逐步脱钩， 出于政治因素、供应链安全、技术路线差异和客户认证体系不同这些原因， 欧美客户大概率不会转而采购中国厂商的产品， 目前Lumentum和Coherent很多产品已经排产到2027甚至2028年， 其中不少订单来自英伟达的提前锁单。
>
> CPO到底有没有真的延期？
> 我倾向于认为没有实质性延期。 
> CPO大致可以分两个阶段看：
> 第一阶段是小规模建设， 2026年下半年开始动工、2027年开始出货， 目前进度仍然按计划推进， 预计英伟达和博通2027年各自的产量都在3万到35万套左右。
> 第二阶段才是真正的大规模放量， 时间点在2028年。 而2027年这一年， NPO(近封装光学)会作为中间过渡方案承接一部分需求。
>
> 网络架构变化会不会减少光模块的需求？
> 市场还担心一件事，像MRC、RNG这类新的网络技术出现后， 会不会减少每台交换机需要的光模块数量。 确实有可能会从原来的6到7个下降到3到4个， 但GPU数量的增长速度远快于这个下降幅度， 整体光学需求预计仍然会持续增长， 这一点担心也偏多余。
>
> 几家公司的财报看点
> Lumentum这次财报压力相对最大， 因为它此前已经给出了市场上最激进的长期指引， 市场关注的是它能不能进一步上调2027年目标， 尤其是单季营收能不能达到20亿美元 (年化80亿美元)、营业利润率能不能超过40%。 Coherent这次是市场机构里比较偏爱的一家， 因为200G EML和高功率激光器的自产比例在持续提升， 加上刚拿到谷歌每年约10亿美元的1.6T模块订单， 以及英伟达2027到2030年的长期采购协议， 未来利润率有望持续改善。 
> AAOI这次财报可能会是营收和指引双双超预期的一份成绩单， 主要动力来自亚马逊和甲骨文的800G订单， 预计二季度收入能超过2亿美元、三季度指引接近3亿美元， 毛利率也会明显高于上半年大约30%的水平。 ANET的增长动力依然强劲， 主要客户覆盖Meta、微软、甲骨文、OpenAI、Anthropic、谷歌， 其中谷歌未来有可能成为它超过10%收入占比的大客户， 大量递延收入预计从2026年下半年开始确认， 带动下半年收入增速超过30%、2027年超过40%。
>
> 这份报告的核心结论
> 总结下来， 中国扩产确实是真实存在的现象， 但短期内不足以改变全球的供需格局。真正具备技术壁垒的200G EML、高功率激光器以及CPO相关产品， 欧美厂商依然领先。2028年仍然是CPO真正大规模放量的时间点， 2027年由NPO承接过渡需求。
> 目前光通信板块的这轮回调更多是情绪和预期驱动， 基本面没有恶化。即将到来的7月底到8月初财报季， 会是验证这条赛道需求是否依然强劲的重要窗口。
>
> 看完这份报告，我想补充一个自己的判断
> 我认为，短期缺货和未来出现结构性过剩并不矛盾（2026 2027年非常看好，2028年以后要注意），这两件事可以同时成立，关键要看过剩最先会出现在哪个环节。
>
> 现在整个行业都看到了AI需求，也都在积极扩产，云厂商也希望引入更多供应商来降低成本、分散供应链风险。如果未来800G、1.6T模块供应商越来越多，ASP下降速度开始快于成本下降速度，那么即使出货量和收入继续增长，毛利率也可能率先承压。
>
> 不过从目前来看，行业还远没有走到这一步。各家公司披露的信息依然指向供给紧张：高端激光器排产排到未来几年，积压订单维持高位，出口限制、良率、客户认证和测试能力仍然是主要瓶颈，真正缺的还是合格的高端产能。
>
> 如果未来行业进入供需再平衡，我认为最先面临价格压力的，大概率还是标准化程度较高的光模块环节，例如400G、逐渐成熟的800G，以及未来进入主流阶段的1.6T产品。像AAOI、中际旭创、新易盛、Source Photonics这类以光模块为主的厂商，未来更需要关注ASP和毛利率的变化。不过这是2028年以后更值得关注的风险，至少在我看来，2026至2027年行业仍然处于供不应求阶段，AAOI等公司依然受益于订单释放、产能爬坡和业绩兑现。
>
> 相比之下，我更看好拥有核心器件壁垒的高端零部件公司，例如Lumentum（LITE）、Coherent（COHR）；以及Ciena（CIEN）、Nokia（NOK）等系统层公司，它们更多依靠技术、网络架构和系统集成能力竞争。至于Veeco（VECO）、Aehr（AEHR）、Viavi（VIAV）等设备和测试公司，只要行业仍在扩产，就有望持续受益于资本开支周期。
>
> 时间线上，我的判断和这份报告基本一致：2026年至2027年上半年仍是供不应求；2027年下半年至2028年，随着新增产能逐步释放，市场会开始重新定价供需关系。
>
> 现在讨论整个光通信行业全面产能过剩还为时过早。未来几年，不同产品、不同技术路线和不同公司，大概率会进入完全不同的供需周期，不会整个行业一起过剩。

### revoAIution (@revoAIution)
_Sat Jul 11 23:15:00 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 36 · ↻ 1 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/revoAIution/status/2076082860138602895)

> Goldman Sachs April 2026 report projects Silicon Photonics growing from 6 percent of the datacom market today to 45 percent by 2028.
>
> Most people read that as a threat to laser companies.
> It is actually the opposite for $SIVE.
>
> Silicon is great at moving light around. But it cannot create light. That is just physics. You always need an external laser feeding light into a Silicon Photonics chip.
> That external laser is what $SIVE makes.
>
> As Silicon Photonics grows from 6 to 45 percent of the market the demand for external CW lasers grows right alongside it.
>
> Goldman basically proved the opposite of what most people assume. More Silicon Photonics means more laser demand. Not less.

### Ernie Milleur (@ErnieMilleur)
_Sat Jul 11 23:58:55 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 2 · ↻ 0 · 💬 2 · [open on X](https://x.com/ErnieMilleur/status/2076093911479796192)

> Quantum Technology: A New Kind of Technology
>
> Quantum technology uses the strange behavior of extremely small particles to create powerful new tools.
>
> Scientists are developing quantum computers, communication systems, and sensors that may someday improve medicine, cybersecurity, navigation, energy, and scientific research.
>
> What Is a Quantum Computer?
>
> Ordinary computers use bits that represent either a zero or a one.
>
> Quantum computers use quantum bits, called qubits. Qubits can behave in unusual ways that may allow a quantum computer to examine certain difficult problems much faster than an ordinary computer.
>
> This does not mean quantum computers will replace phones, laptops, or regular computers. They are being designed for special problems that are extremely difficult to solve.
>
> How Could Quantum Computers Help?
>
> Quantum computers may eventually help scientists:
>
> Discover new medicines
> Design stronger materials
> Improve batteries
> Study complicated molecules
> Plan transportation routes
> Develop cleaner energy
> Understand diseases
> Improve weather and climate research
>
> Many of these possibilities are still being tested. Quantum computers are not yet powerful or reliable enough to perform most of these tasks better than ordinary computers.
>
> Why Are Quantum Computers So Difficult to Build?
>
> Qubits are extremely fragile.
>
> Heat, vibration, electrical interference, and tiny manufacturing errors can disturb them. Some quantum computers must be kept at temperatures colder than outer space.
>
> Scientists are working to reduce errors and keep quantum information stable long enough to complete useful calculations.
>
> Quantum Sensors
>
> Quantum sensors may become useful sooner than large quantum computers.
>
> These sensors can make extremely precise measurements. They may help doctors see inside the body, help ships or aircraft navigate when GPS is unavailable, locate objects underground, monitor the environment, and improve scientific research.
>
> Atomic clocks are an example of quantum technology already being used today. They help support GPS, communications, banking, and other important systems.
>
> Quantum Communication
>
> Quantum communication may provide new ways to protect sensitive information.
>
> It can use the laws of quantum physics to reveal whether someone has attempted to intercept a message.
>
> However, no communication system is completely secure. Computers, software, passwords, and human mistakes can still create weaknesses.
>
> Could Quantum Computers Break Encryption?
>
> A powerful future quantum computer may be able to break some of the encryption currently protecting websites, financial systems, government information, and private communications.
>
> Present quantum computers cannot do this on a large scale.
>
> Governments and technology companies are already developing new forms of encryption designed to withstand future quantum attacks. This is called post-quantum cryptography.
>
> Is Quantum Technology Being Exaggerated?
>
> There is genuine progress, although there is also a great deal of publicity and exaggeration.
>
> Companies sometimes announce impressive numbers of qubits without clearly explaining how reliable those qubits are. A machine with many unstable qubits may be less useful than a smaller and more accurate machine.
>
> Promises about instant medical cures, unbeatable artificial intelligence, or computers that solve every problem should be treated carefully.
>
> Why Does This Matter?
>
> Quantum technology could eventually improve medicine, strengthen cybersecurity, create better materials, support cleaner energy, and provide more accurate measuring tools.
>
> It could also increase military competition, threaten older encryption, and give powerful countries or corporations greater technological control.
>
> Quantum technology is not magic, and it is not ready to transform everyday life immediately. It is an important developing field that may gradually change science, security, medicine, and industry.
>
> The wisest response is neither fear nor blind excitement. We should follow its progress carefully, prepare for its risks, and use its discoveries responsibly.
>
> Quantum technology seeks to control some of the smallest and strangest features of nature and turn them into useful machines.
>
> The field includes far more than futuristic computers. It also includes extraordinarily sensitive measuring instruments, highly accurate clocks, secure communication methods, and networks that may someday connect quantum devices across great distances.
>
> The three most developed areas are quantum computing, quantum communication, and quantum sensing. Each uses the laws of quantum mechanics differently, and each is progressing at a different speed.
>
> What Makes Something Quantum?
>
> Ordinary computers store and process information using bits. A bit represents either a zero or a one.
>
> A quantum computer uses quantum bits, usually called qubits. Under controlled conditions, a qubit can exist in a combination of possible states known as superposition. Multiple qubits can also become entangled, meaning their properties are connected in ways that cannot be fully explained by treating each particle separately.
>
> Quantum algorithms manipulate these combined possibilities through interference. Some possible answers are strengthened, while others are weakened or canceled. When the qubits are measured, however, the delicate quantum state collapses into an ordinary result.
>
> This does not mean that a quantum computer simply tries every possible answer at once and instantly selects the correct one. That popular explanation is too simplistic. A useful quantum algorithm must be carefully designed so that interference makes the desired information more likely to appear when the system is measured.
>
> The Problem of Quantum Fragility
>
> Quantum states are extremely delicate.
>
> Heat, vibration, electromagnetic interference, imperfect controls, microscopic manufacturing defects, and interactions with the surrounding environment can introduce errors. The loss of usable quantum behavior is known as decoherence.
>
> Some quantum computers therefore operate inside elaborate refrigeration systems at temperatures close to absolute zero. Other designs use trapped ions, neutral atoms, photons, semiconductor devices, or other physical systems.
>
> Each approach has advantages and weaknesses. Researchers have not yet established one universally superior form of quantum hardware.
>
> The number of qubits also tells only part of the story. A machine containing many unreliable qubits may accomplish less than one containing fewer, higher-quality qubits. Important measurements include error rates, connectivity, operating speed, coherence time, and the complexity of circuits the machine can execute accurately.
>
> Quantum Error Correction
>
> A fully useful quantum computer will probably require quantum error correction.
>
> Because unknown quantum information cannot simply be copied like an ordinary computer file, error correction must distribute information across groups of physical qubits. Together, these physical qubits form a more dependable logical qubit.
>
> This process requires substantial hardware. Depending on the quality of the components and the error-correction method, one reliable logical qubit may require many physical qubits.
>
> Progress in error correction is therefore often more meaningful than announcements based only on total qubit counts. The central challenge is not merely constructing a larger processor. It is making the entire system more reliable as it grows.
>
> Quantum Computing
>
> Quantum computers are specialized machines intended to perform certain calculations using quantum effects.
>
> They are not expected to replace laptops, phones, conventional servers, or supercomputers. Most daily tasks—including word processing, video playback, email, accounting, web browsing, and database management—are handled more efficiently by ordinary computers.
>
> The more realistic future is hybrid computing. Conventional processors will manage most of a workload, while a quantum processor may be assigned a narrow calculation for which it offers a genuine advantage.
>
> IBM, for example, has published plans for closer integration between quantum systems and classical supercomputers, along with tools for monitoring and debugging hybrid workloads. These are company roadmaps rather than guarantees of when broad commercial advantage will arrive.
>
> Promising Uses of Quantum Computers
>
> Chemistry and medicine
>
> Nature is quantum mechanical at the molecular level. Simulating molecules accurately becomes extremely difficult for classical computers as their complexity increases.
>
> Future quantum computers may help scientists model chemical reactions, proteins, catalysts, and pharmaceutical compounds. This could support drug discovery, although quantum computers would not eliminate laboratory testing, clinical trials, safety reviews, or the biological complexity of disease.
>
> Materials and energy
>
> Quantum simulation may help researchers investigate improved batteries, superconductors, fertilizers, solar materials, industrial catalysts, and methods of capturing carbon.
>
> Even modest improvements in catalysts could reduce the energy required by major industrial processes. The difficulty is reaching a scale and accuracy that outperform the best classical methods on genuinely valuable problems.
>
> Optimization
>
> Organizations face complicated scheduling, routing, manufacturing, investment, and supply-chain problems.
>
> Quantum algorithms may eventually help with certain forms of optimization. However, many optimization claims remain experimental. Classical algorithms also continue to improve, so a quantum method must be compared with the strongest conventional alternative rather than an outdated one.
>
> Scientific discovery
>
> Quantum computers may become valuable research instruments for nuclear physics, high-energy physics, materials science, and other fields involving complex quantum systems.
>
> The Department of Energy has identified quantum information science as relevant to materials research, environmental measurement, navigation, dark-matter searches, gravitational-wave detection, and other scientific challenges.
>
> Artificial intelligence
>
> Quantum computing and artificial intelligence may eventually complement one another. AI can help calibrate quantum devices, analyze experimental results, and search for improved control methods.
>
> Quantum algorithms might someday accelerate selected machine-learning calculations. Claims that quantum computers will automatically make all AI dramatically more powerful remain unproven.
>
> Quantum Communication
>
> Quantum communication transfers or shares information using quantum states, often carried by photons.
>
> One important concept is quantum key distribution. It can allow two parties to create encryption keys while detecting certain attempts to intercept the quantum transmission. Measurement disturbs quantum states, so eavesdropping can leave detectable evidence.
>
> Quantum key distribution does not make an entire communication system invulnerable. Hardware, software, users, authentication systems, and network endpoints can still be attacked.
>
> Researchers are also working toward quantum networks that could connect sensors, processors, memories, and communication devices. Entanglement might eventually be distributed across these networks, enabling capabilities that ordinary networks cannot reproduce. NIST is developing components, prototypes, and test beds for quantum networking.
>
> A large-scale “quantum internet” remains a long-term research goal. It would not simply be a faster version of today’s internet. It would likely operate alongside classical networks and provide specialized functions.
>
> Quantum Sensing
>
> Quantum sensing may affect society sooner than large fault-tolerant quantum computing.
>
> Quantum sensors use properties such as atomic energy levels, spin, interference, and entanglement to measure time, gravity, magnetic fields, acceleration, rotation, temperature, and other physical quantities with exceptional precision.
>
> Some quantum-based instruments already exist. Atomic clocks support precise timekeeping, navigation, telecommunications, scientific measurement, and the operation of modern infrastructure.
>
> Emerging quantum sensors may help locate underground structures, detect subtle magnetic signals, improve medical imaging, monitor environmental changes, measure movement without relying entirely on GPS, and conduct fundamental scientific experiments.
>
> Quantum sensing often does not require the enormous error-corrected processors needed for universal quantum computing. This may allow useful sensing products to mature earlier.
>
> Navigation Without GPS
>
> Modern transportation, communications, finance, energy systems, and military operations depend heavily upon accurate timing and satellite navigation.
>
> Quantum accelerometers, gyroscopes, clocks, and gravimeters could contribute to navigation systems that continue operating when GPS signals are blocked, jammed, unavailable, or unreliable.
>
> Such systems would not necessarily make satellites unnecessary. They could provide an additional layer of resilience for aircraft, ships, emergency services, research vessels, infrastructure, and national defense.
>
> The Encryption Challenge
>
> A sufficiently powerful fault-tolerant quantum computer could threaten widely used public-key cryptographic systems.
>
> These systems help protect websites, financial transactions, government communications, software updates, digital identities, and private records. The danger does not mean present quantum machines can suddenly break all modern encryption. They cannot.
>
> The concern is partly long-term. An attacker could collect encrypted information today and retain it until future technology becomes capable of decrypting it. This is sometimes described as “harvest now, decrypt later.”
>
> The principal defense is post-quantum cryptography: conventional mathematical encryption designed to resist attacks from both classical and quantum computers.
>
> Moving to new cryptographic systems takes years because organizations must identify vulnerable systems, update software and hardware, test compatibility, replace long-lived equipment, and protect archived information. Preparation should therefore begin before a cryptographically dangerous quantum computer exists.
>
> Quantum communication and post-quantum cryptography should not be confused. One uses quantum physical systems; the other generally runs on conventional computers.
>
> Where the Field Stands in 2026
>
> Quantum research has entered a period of large public and private investment.
>
> In November 2025, the U.S. Department of Energy announced $625 million to renew five National Quantum Information Science Research Centers. IBM announced in June 2026 that it planned to invest more than $10 billion in quantum computing over five years. These commitments show strategic confidence in the field, although investment does not guarantee that every technical roadmap will be achieved on schedule.
>
> Researchers are improving control systems, fabrication, modular architectures, networking, software, and error-correction techniques. Companies are also attempting to integrate quantum processors with classical high-performance computing.
>
> At the same time, the field remains vulnerable to exaggerated announcements. Experimental demonstrations may solve artificial benchmark problems without producing immediate commercial value. Company claims can also face scientific dispute, as recent criticism of Microsoft’s topological-qubit research illustrates.
>
> Responsible evaluation requires published evidence, independent replication, meaningful benchmarks, and comparison with the best available classical machines.
>
> Major Obstacles
>
> Noise and errors
>
> Qubits lose information and accumulate errors rapidly. Useful computation may require far greater reliability than most present systems provide.
>
> Scaling
>
> A laboratory device containing a small number of controllable qubits is very different from an industrial system containing enough logical qubits for valuable fault-tolerant computation.
>
> Manufacturing
>
> Quantum hardware requires extraordinary precision. Tiny variations can affect the behavior of individual qubits and reduce production yield.
>
> Cooling and infrastructure
>
> Some architectures require complex cryogenic equipment, shielding, lasers, vacuum systems, control electronics, or specialized facilities.
>
> Software
>
> Quantum programming demands new algorithms, compilers, verification methods, and ways to divide work between quantum and classical processors.
>
> Verification
>
> A difficult question arises when a quantum computer produces a result that no classical computer can independently reproduce. Researchers need trustworthy methods to verify the calculation.
>
> Cost
>
> Quantum systems remain expensive to build, operate, maintain, and calibrate. Early access will probably be concentrated in governments, universities, cloud providers, and large companies.
>
> Economic and Social Effects
>
> Quantum technology may create demand for physicists, engineers, programmers, technicians, mathematicians, cybersecurity specialists, materials scientists, and manufacturing workers.
>
> The field also requires people who can connect scientific research with medicine, chemistry, business, law, ethics, and public policy.
>
> Not every worker will need a doctorate in quantum physics. A mature industry will also require conventional software development, electronics, refrigeration, photonics, fabrication, maintenance, education, sales, and regulatory expertise.
>
> At the same time, unequal access could concentrate scientific and economic power among a small number of countries and companies. Public research, education, shared infrastructure, international standards, and responsible cloud access may help broaden participation.
>
> Military and Geopolitical Concerns
>
> Quantum technology has implications for secure communication, navigation, surveillance, sensing, codebreaking, submarine detection, and advanced materials.
>
> This makes it strategically important to governments. It also increases the danger of secrecy, international rivalry, export restrictions, and an expensive technological arms race.
>
> Quantum research has many peaceful uses, yet the same capability may have both civilian and military applications. Nations will need to protect legitimate security interests while maintaining enough scientific cooperation to support safety, verification, and responsible standards.
>
> Ethical Questions
>
> Quantum technology raises several important questions:
>
> Who should control the most powerful systems?
>
> How should governments prevent misuse without blocking beneficial research?
>
> How should claims of “quantum advantage” be tested?
>
> How can society avoid wasting public money on hype?
>
> How should privacy be protected during the transition to quantum-resistant security?
>
> How can smaller nations, universities, and businesses participate without becoming permanently dependent on a few providers?
>
> These questions should be addressed while the technology is developing, rather than after its effects become difficult to reverse.
>
> What Quantum Technology Will Not Do
>
> Quantum technology will not make every computer program faster.
>
> It will not instantly cure disease, predict the future, eliminate uncertainty, make artificial intelligence all-knowing, or solve every mathematical problem.
>
> Quantum entanglement does not permit ordinary information to travel faster than light.
>
> Quantum computers also do not test every possibility and effortlessly reveal the correct answer. Their advantages depend upon particular algorithms, suitable hardware, low error rates, and problems whose structure can be exploited quantum mechanically.
>
> Any claim that ignores these limitations should be treated cautiously.
>
> A Realistic Outlook
>
> Quantum sensing and timing are likely to deliver practical benefits earlier and more widely than universal fault-tolerant quantum computing.
>
> Quantum communication will probably develop through specialized networks, government systems, research links, and security-sensitive applications before becoming broadly available.
>
> Quantum computing may progress through increasingly capable hybrid systems. The decisive milestone will not be a dramatic qubit announcement. It will be the repeated solution of useful problems more accurately, quickly, or economically than the best classical alternatives.
>
> That transition may be gradual. Classical computers will also continue advancing, creating a moving target that quantum systems must surpass.
>
> Why Quantum Technology Matters to Ordinary People
>
> Most people may never own a quantum computer, just as most people do not own a supercomputer or an atomic clock.
>
> They may still benefit from the technology indirectly.
>
> Quantum tools could contribute to safer medicines, stronger materials, improved batteries, more accurate medical instruments, resilient navigation, earlier detection of underground hazards, better scientific models, and stronger digital security.
>
> They could also create risks if governments and businesses fail to modernize encryption, test claims carefully, control military applications responsibly, or ensure fair access.
>
> Quantum technology should therefore be approached with neither blind excitement nor automatic fear. It is a serious developing field with genuine achievements, extraordinary possibilities, unresolved scientific barriers, and a large amount of uncertainty.
>
> Its eventual influence will depend not only upon what researchers are able to build, but also upon the wisdom with which society chooses to use it.

**Media**
- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HM_EZY6bEAAwEcS.jpg
