### Milk Road AI (@MilkRoadAI)
_Sun Jul 05 20:27:01 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 48 · ↻ 10 · 💬 8 · [open on X](https://x.com/MilkRoadAI/status/2073866260476277007)

> The silicon photonics supply chain diagram is one of the most important investment maps in technology right now (Save this).
>
> Every AI data center being built depends on what's in that chart and the companies inside it are just starting to show what the revenue ramp looks like.
>
> Here are the 10 stocks I am watching.
>
> 1. Broadcom (AVGO): Broadcom's AI revenue rocketed 106% to $8.4 billion in its most recent quarter, driven by custom accelerator chips for Google, Meta, and Anthropic, plus AI networking silicon. It is one of the few companies doing both the switch silicon and the photonics integration needed for co-packaged optics at hyperscale. The silicon photonics diagram shows Broadcom appearing across multiple layers, PIC design, laser sources, photodiode, and EIC design.
>
> 2. MACOM Technology (MTSI): MACOM is quietly positioning itself at the inflection point of the 1.6T and 3.2T optical transceiver transition. In March 2026 it launched 448G PAM4 modulator drivers among the first in the industry and joined Broadcom, Cisco, and Semtech in the 400G Optical MSA standards consortium. In June 2026 it introduced hot via chip scale technology, eliminating wire bonds in its AlGaAs packaging.
>
> 3. Marvell Technology (MRVL): Marvell is the DSP engine inside many of the optical modules in that chart. Its custom AI silicon, built for hyperscalers who want to own their accelerator architecture is the fastest growing part of its business. It sits at the EIC design layer and supplies the digital signal processing that makes high-speed optical links work reliably at scale. As the industry shifts from 400G to 800G and 1.6T, every step requires more sophisticated DSPs and Marvell captures more revenue per module shipped.
>
> 4. Keysight Technologies (KEYS): Every optical module that ships from every fab in that chart has to be tested before it reaches a data center. Keysight is the global leader in electronic and photonic test equipment. As optical speeds push to 800G and beyond, the testing instrumentation has to keep pace and it commands premium pricing.
>
> 5. FormFactor (FORM): FormFactor is the most underappreciated name in this entire chart. Q1 2026 revenue was $226 million, up 32% year over year, beating estimates with non-GAAP EPS of $0.56 versus $0.44 expected. It acquired Keystone Photonics in December 2025, becoming the leading wafer-level silicon photonics test platform for co-packaged optics production. Its partnership with Advantest created the world's fastest automated photonic alignment test system with nine-axis nano-precision. Over 100 of the world's leading silicon photonics manufacturers use FormFactor systems meaning every CPO chip that ships from any fab in that diagram gets tested on FormFactor equipment.
>
> 6. Teradyne (TER): Teradyne sits in the E/O Testing layer alongside Keysight and FormFactor. As silicon photonics chips get more complex, integrating lasers, modulators, photodetectors and electronic drivers on a single chip,  the test complexity explodes. Teradyne's automated test equipment platforms are expanding from traditional semiconductor testing into photonic integrated circuit validation. It also has a robotics division, which ties the silicon photonics thesis directly back to the humanoid supply chain story.
>
> 7. EXFO (EXFO): EXFO is a fiber optic and network testing specialist that has been building testing platforms specifically for coherent optical and silicon photonics applications. It sits directly in the E/O Testing box of the supply chain map. It's a smaller cap, which means the upside from the optical buildout is amplified relative to its size. It is one of the few companies that tests live network optical performance meaning it gets pulled in not just at the component manufacturing stage but every time a data center expands or upgrades.
>
> 8. Foxconn Industrial Internet (FXCOF): Foxconn appears twice in that supply chain diagram in both Photonics Assembly and Optical Interconnect and that is before you even consider its server business. Q1 2026 revenue hit $66.6 billion, up 29.7% year over year, with AI servers now representing more than 50% of total server revenue. Its silicon photonics CPO switches entered mass production in Q3 2026 with full year shipments forecast at 10,000 units. It is boosting capex 30% specifically for AI infrastructure. Almost no retail investors think of Foxconn as a silicon photonics play and that's the opportunity.
>
> 9. Sumitomo Electric (SMTOY): Sumitomo appears in two places on that supply chain diagram as an optical interconnect component supplier and in the laser/photodiode layer. The company has been a foundational supplier to the fiber optic industry for decades and is now scaling its silicon photonics packaging and optical connectivity capabilities for AI data center applications.
>
> 10. Synopsys (SNPS): Every silicon photonics chip has to be designed before it can be manufactured. Synopsys is the dominant EDA software company for photonic integrated circuit design and sits at the very top left of that supply chain map. The shift toward co-packaged optics means optical and electronic chip design have to be co-simulated, exactly the kind of complex, multi physics workflow Synopsys is built for. Its photonics design tools are already embedded across every major chip company in that diagram. The more complex the chip, the more customers pay for Synopsys tools.
>
> Milk Road Pro is tracking every layer of the silicon photonics supply chain, from Broadcom and Marvell to the testing names most investors still don’t know.
>
> Join Milk Road Pro for the full breakdown and for all our AI trades for just $1 using  the link below!

>

>

>

>

>
> 3.$SNDK (Enterprise Data Lakes): As companies move from training AI to running inference on massive datasets, the demand for enterprise-grade NAND (storage) will explode. $SNDK is positioned to capture the shift toward high-density, low-power storage required for 2030-era data centers.

### Cassius Au Bellona (@SpaceExplorer30)
_Sun Jul 05 20:41:46 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 3 · ↻ 0 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/SpaceExplorer30/status/2073869971986198731)

> Mapping $SIVE 2030:
>
> Current: ~52 SEK 
>
> 2030 Target: 260 SEK 
>
> Cap: ~85B SEK
>
> The catalyst is the AI Power Wall. As copper interconnects fail, Sivers photonics becomes the standard for data center light sources. A pure play on the transition from hardware to AI infrastructure.
>
> For $SIVE, the 2030 re-rating is a bet on the "Optical Transition." Right now, the market sees them as a niche small-cap component maker. By 2030, they have the potential to be the standard-bearer for light-source technology in AI clusters.
> Here is why I believe the bull case for a ~260 SEK target is realistic:
>
> 1.The Silicon Photonics (SiPh) Shift: Data centers are hitting a "Power Wall." Traditional copper wires generate too much heat and lose too much signal at AI scale. Moving data with light (photonics) is 1,000x more efficient. Sivers Photonics produces the high-power DFB lasers that act as the "engine" for these optical interconnects.
>
> 2.The LEO Satellite Explosion: Beyond AI, their beamforming chips are core to the Low Earth Orbit (LEO) satellite market. As global internet coverage shifts to space, the demand for low-cost, high-efficiency ground and satellite terminals will move from thousands to millions of units.
>
> 3.The 6G Infrastructure Bridge: As we move toward 2030, the 6G standard will rely heavily on mmWave technology. Sivers has been refining this tech for years while others were focused only on standard 5G. They own the "hard part" of the spectrum.
> If they successfully navigate the liquidity hurdles of the next few years, the "massive gap" you see is the market finally pricing them as a critical infrastructure provider rather than a speculative hardware play.

### TheBigBerbowski (@TheBigBerbowski)
_Sun Jul 05 21:01:19 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 34 · ↻ 1 · 💬 5 · [open on X](https://x.com/TheBigBerbowski/status/2073874893205106881)

> I'm seeing it every day. 
>
> Investors comparing their YTD, YoY performance, and even weekly/daily performance. 
>
> It's really not fair to compare apples and pumpkins. 
>
> - Investor investing in cyclical companies will definitely go up and down based on the cycle and timing.
> - Investor investing in high growth will perform during low rates but struggle during inflation.
> - Investor investing in value will miss huge runs but they focus on safety.
> - Investing in biotech, pharma, car, energy industry all brings different outcomes. If car industry is lagging, it's impossible to expect an SME for this industry to find 10 baggers in photonics. 
>
> That's just one piece of the story. 
>
> The next one is about your investing style or strategy.
> - Long?
> - Day/swing trading? 
> - Using options? 
> - Using all of the above? 
>
> In a volatile environment swing trader should have more options and long investors may underperform. If the market has bearish outlook, shorters may have more luck than the rest?
>
> We can't compare traders in robotics vs long term investors in consumer staples. Makes no sense. 
>
> There's the last piece of the story. 
>
> Not everyone is having the same amount of cash available, nor the same risk tolerance, nor the same time horizon, nor time commitment.  
>
> One investor has a difficult work and no time to pay attention to daily movements. He can't really go and day trade or swing trade. 
> Another one with 5 billion portfolio cannot have 50% in a single month. He is likely happy with 3%. 
> A student having 200 usd to throw in $SIVE and getting 5x cannot be compared to someone managing his family portfolio. 
>
> When you next time compare yourself with someone, make sure to understand these three dimensions. 
>
> It's VERY likely the guy you're comparing yourself with has different investing profile and strategy. Maybe he isn't investing in memory and buying selling every day. 
>
> Only compare your current performance to your own last month or last year. 
>
> Competing with oneself is one of the most effective paths to sustained personal growth in anything you do.
>
> TBB

### mark (@cherryPayment)
_Sun Jul 05 21:42:40 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 15 · ↻ 1 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/cherryPayment/status/2073885296807346457)

> 我写过 Soitec、SIVE、IQE、Shunsin、AAOI……很多人把它们当成各自独立的票。但如果你把这些环节摊在一张桌子上,会发现一个几乎没人问过的问题:它们最后,是在谁的工厂里被"连起来"造出来的?
>
> 今天我们来聊一下这家快被遗忘的欧洲小厂: $XFAB的故事。 先说几个我一直都觉得很有意思的点:
>
> 1. 首先它的出身就带有历史性意味，它是 1992 年从"东德解体后被拆分的电子工业巨头"里长出来的, 然后被一批比利时人接手, 而这批比利时人还顺手创办了另一家汽车芯片龙头 Melexis，这意味着同一批人,一手造芯片、一手造工厂。
>
> 2. 它不卷纳米, 却能够把英伟达和诺基亚拉进了自己的局。 它牵头的一个欧盟出钱的硅光子项目中英伟达、诺基亚、imec 都是同桌的参与方。 一家欧洲小代工厂,能召集起这种阵容,本身就说明问题。
>
> 3. 它可能是我这一整条硅光/CPO 链的"总枢纽"。 它在 Soitec 的 SOI 地基上、用 SMART Photonics 的 InP,造出喂给 AAOI 的硅光芯片;同时又是 NVTS 那条"电"线上的 SiC 代工龙头，一只手 AI 光、一只手 EV 电。 
>
> 但真正让我觉得很神奇的点在于它约六成的股份,锁在两个创始家族和一个州政府手里，但我们需要知道为什么是这样？而这样又意味着什么？ 
>
> 如果你感兴趣可以在substack上阅读全文，我把链接放在下面了，谢谢
>
> https://t.co/0zw7pMaZCq

### Eidolon Research (@EidolonResearch)
_Sun Jul 05 23:06:23 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 6 · ↻ 1 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/EidolonResearch/status/2073906365119295945)

> Bullish $SIVE: AMD is building CPO for the MI500 (2027) through GlobalFoundries, bypassing NVIDIA’s TSMC packaging bottleneck entirely. Since June, Sivers’ laser arrays are integrated into GF’s silicon photonics reference designs and SCALE CPO platform. If AMD’s optical scale-up bet materializes at GF, Sivers lasers are in the supply chain. NVIDIA stumbling widens exactly the window AMD and its photonics partners need.
>
> Bullish $AAOI: every year CPO slips at NVIDIA is another year pluggable transceivers remain the workhorse of AI datacenters. Delays don’t destroy optical demand, they redirect capital back to pluggables and NPO. That’s AAOI’s core business. The market dumped it 17% on the delay headline without asking who actually benefits from it.
>
> One company wins if CPO accelerates outside NVIDIA. The other wins because it’s delayed inside NVIDIA. Both win from the same news.
>
> Delays don’t kill demand. They redistribute it.

### BankofVol Grift¹⁰⁰⁰🤖🤖¹⁰⁰⁰⁰⁰⁰ (@BankofVol)
_Sun Jul 05 23:34:34 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 15 · ↻ 2 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/BankofVol/status/2073913459134103592)

> — Kyber NVL144, the flagship 2027 rack, delayed 12+ months to 2028. The PCB midplane can’t be manufactured at scale
> — The backup architecture (NVL72x2) — cancelled
> — The 4-die Rubin Ultra was already dead: packaging physically warps at that size. The 2-die survivor delivers roughly half the performance per package
> — Optical scale-up (CPO) won’t arrive until Feynman
>
> This is not one product slipping. It’s two physical walls — packaging AND interconnect — hitting in the same cycle. The “new rack every year” promise is what’s breaking.
>
> WINNERS
>
> — $GOOGL / $AVGO — the only proven alternative scale-up architecture on earth (optical switching, running in production for years). The 2027 window belongs to the TPU ecosystem
> — $AMD — gets a window. A window is not a win. Execution at rack scale is unproven
> — Pluggable optics: $COHR, $FN, $AAOI — CPO was the sword hanging over pluggables. It just got sheathed for another generation. The recent photonics selloff shot the wrong victim
> — Copper: $APH, $CRDO — copper stays in the rack longer than anyone modeled
> — Neoclouds: $NBIS, $CRWV — slower chip cadence means GPU fleets obsolete slower. The depreciation treadmill every bear cites just lost a year
>
> LOSERS
>
> — $NVDA — not revenue. They’ll sell every mature-gen rack they can make. What’s damaged is the moat premium: NVLink supremacy and the annual cadence ARE the multiple
> — CPO pure plays: $POET, Sivers — the entire thesis is co-packaged optics adoption timing. That timing just moved right by a full generation. The biggest losers (Ayar Labs, Celestial AI) are private — you can’t even trade them
> — $LITE — the trap. CPO laser story delayed, pluggable laser business extended. Net wash. Not the short people will think it is
>
> THE $MU QUESTION
>
> Do the math before you touch the sell button. Old Kyber rack: 144 packages x 16 HBM stacks = 2,304. New 2+2 config: 288 packages x 8 stacks = 2,304. Bit demand per rack: identical. What died is the “HBM per GPU doubles forever” narrative — a multiple story, not a bits story. And a flatter performance curve means buyers need MORE units for the same compute, in a market that’s supply-constrained until 2028.
>
> Neutral on fundamentals. If it does trade down on the headline, then that gap will be called opportunity.
>
> The nuance everyone will miss: NVIDIA can still hit rack-level compute targets with 2+2. Parity — bought with twice the silicon. The spec sheet survives. Cost per FLOP doesn’t.
>
> The only question for 2027: can anyone exploit the gap before Feynman closes it? Exactly one company has a working alternative today.
>
> Not financial advice.

### Karthik Senthil (@karsenthil)
_Tue Jul 07 15:53:49 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 5 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/karsenthil/status/2074522281905099260)

> Thoughts on the market and opportunities I see:
> - Lot of FUD in the AI trade right now. This is healthy for the market. Many "bottlenecks" were hyped up (like photonics) and got overextended. Still remain ultra-bullish on memory for the next 6-12 months. Yes at some point, the supply/demand capacity imbalance will normalize but that will happen at the earliest in 2028.  Yes, there will be optimizations to how much memory is required both for model training and inference. But inference demand will grow massively especially as token price goes down which will make these companies not nearly as cyclical as they have been in the past.  Network effects here are underrated.
> - The big opportunity in the AI trade is the orchestration layer. The layer that can execute user intent in a way that optimizes across cost, power, model capability, privacy, and latency.  The future wont require users to know model series or if they should use cloud provider A or neocloud B. I dont yet know who will win this but if they can focus, $AAPL is the best positioned because they are vertically integrated especially across devices (phone, tablet, airpods) and don't have a frontier lab they have to give preference to.
> - Crypto is underpriced right now. The two big opportunities IMO are SoV (BTC/ZEC) and a way to create + run inference on models in a way that's not dependent on governments or OAI/Anthropic. As these labs get more nationalized, just like Bitcoin was an opt-out for people on government-issued money, accessing a distributed trained frontier model represents the same opt-out.  The technology is almost here to enable this, super exciting times (will write more about this in a future post)

### 👁 (@yogigundogdu)
_Tue Jul 07 16:19:28 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 1 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/yogigundogdu/status/2074528736956096610)

> Relax. Touch grass. Go find some extra cash.
>
> $META isn’t waving the white flag on AI. They’re building a cloud business to monetize excess AI compute capacity. This is exactly what you do when your infrastructure investments are working and you have more power than you need internally right now. It’s a feature, not a bug. The market just spun it as oversupply panic.
>
> On the $NVDA side, the comments around Kyber rack delays and some architecture tweaks are real noise. But Nvidia’s core roadmap stays intact. Rubin moves into broader availability in the second half of this year. Ultra and the following platform come in 2027-2028. No serious competitor catches up in high-performance AI accelerators before then. Every major model provider and hyperscaler is trying to build their own custom chips, but those won’t be available at meaningful scale until 2028. Custom silicon from the big clouds remains complementary for now.
>
> Memory chips (especially HBM): AI data centers are still on track to swallow around 70 percent of global memory production in 2026. HBM is sold out through the year across $SKHY, Samsung, and $MU. This is a genuine supercycle.
> AI data center buildout keeps accelerating. Hyperscalers are guiding for hundreds of billions in capex this year. The physical infrastructure demand for power, cooling, and space is only increasing.
>
> Any increased focus on open models could ultimately prove very positive for the industry. Inference workloads from on-demand open models will drive demand for efficient, low-cost compute at specialized data centers. Providers like $NBIS and $IREN are well positioned here because they deliver cheap power and purpose-built infrastructure that these models will depend on. 
>
> As noted on the All-In podcast, David Friedberg has highlighted that AI cloud services could host the majority of workloads (around 70 percent in his view), while local hosting persists and is not going away, especially with open models running on demand.
>
> Photonics demand grows with the need for better efficiency. Co-packaged optics and silicon photonics solve power and bandwidth limits inside and across racks. Even with some near-term rack timeline shifts, the structural requirement for optical interconnects rises as clusters get larger.
>
> Existing connected and powered capacity remains valuable. Volume ramps may shift later than some models assumed, but that just gives more time to accumulate quality names in memory, data center infrastructure, and photonics-related plays.
>
> Hyperscaler earnings are coming up soon. Capex commentary will tell the real story. The music is still playing?

### The Tycoon Mindset (@tycoonmindset05)
_Tue Jul 07 17:54:50 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 2 · ↻ 0 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/tycoonmindset05/status/2074552736331542977)

> The Biggest AI Opportunity Isn't Always the Chip
>
> Whenever AI is discussed, companies like NVIDIA usually dominate the conversation. Everyone wants faster GPUs, more computing power and larger AI models.
>
> But there's another problem quietly becoming just as important - moving data between those chips. As AI models become larger, the amount of information flowing inside data centres is exploding. 
>
> Traditional copper connections are slowly reaching their limits, and that's where the industry is turning towards silicon photonics, which uses light instead of electricity to move data much faster.

**Media**
- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HMpGpjSbwAALpkS.jpg

### The Tycoon Mindset (@tycoonmindset05)
_Tue Jul 07 17:54:51 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 5 · ↻ 0 · 💬 2 · [open on X](https://x.com/tycoonmindset05/status/2074552741503050160)

> So Where Does IZMO Fit In?
>
> This is where many investors misunderstand the story.
> IZMO is not trying to manufacture AI chips. Instead, it is building one of the most critical parts that allows those chips to work efficiently - advanced semiconductor packaging and silicon photonics packaging. 
>
> In simple words, even the most powerful chip is of little use if it cannot communicate quickly with the rest of the system.
>
> What's interesting is that as semiconductor technology becomes more complex, packaging itself is becoming increasingly valuable. Management shared that while traditional packaging contributes only 8-10% of a chip's value, advanced packaging contributes around 50%, and silicon photonics packaging can account for almost 80%. That is a remarkable shift in where value is being created.

**Media**
- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HMpHKIebYAE73D9.png

### The Tycoon Mindset (@tycoonmindset05)
_Tue Jul 07 17:54:52 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 3 · ↻ 0 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/tycoonmindset05/status/2074552746192277991)

> A Small Business Today, But Management's Ambition Is Much Bigger
>
> At the moment, IzmoMicro is still a relatively small business. It generated around ₹18-19 crore of revenue in FY26, but management expects this to increase to ₹45-50 crore in FY27.
>
> More importantly, the building blocks are gradually falling into place. The company already has an order book of around ₹40 crore, a pipeline of nearly ₹100 crore, partnerships with IIT Madras, Alcyon Photonics and CCRAFT, and has established a presence in Germany to access European semiconductor customers. 
>
> Management's long-term aspiration is to build IzmoMicro into a ₹1,200-1,500 crore business over the next five years.

### Joshua Fong. CFA. (@JoshuaFong_X)
_Tue Jul 07 18:04:38 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/JoshuaFong_X/status/2074555201873379479)

> Market Review (Mid-Day) 20260707:
> - Semi and Memory washout this morning, BUT still trying to hang in there. Basically all the prior hardware leading sectors, including Photonics, Data Centres etc.
> - I've been banging the drum about money rotating OUT of AI HARDWARE for about 2 weeks now. So this is no surprise. The AI Trade is NOT over. I just see money rotating now to the next layer. 
> - Where? Remember I talked about Cybersecurity and selected software? It is becoming clearer that it is mostly storage and database management related. That is why DELL, HPE, NTAP, SNOW, DDOG, RBRK, all continue to do well. These guys STORE and MANAGE the Data. And then we have CRWD PANW FTNT. These guys PROTECT the data. RDDT seems to be ok too. They have a lot of data. 
> - See what is the common denominator? DATA. At the end of the day, AI needs data to function to its best ability. And that data needs to be stored and managed properly. 
> - There is another layer on top of the Data layer, which is usage / application. Biotech is a clear beneficiary and that's why its been leading recently. Fintech seems to take to it easily as well, and has been doing well too. 
> - Interestingly, one of my favourite companies at the moment, ZETA, play both in the DATA and benefits from USAGE. But it’s a very volatile small cap. Not for everyone. 
> - So, what now?
> - I don’t know your investment horizon. If long enough, the AI hardware trade I think will come back at some point. It needs to base and rest and for now. Just beware that often, distribution / topping sometimes looks like basing / resting. We only know after the fact. So we have to bear that in mind as a possible scenario. What I am saying is that, using Memory as an example, it is POSSIBLE that it has topped. I do not know and don't want to call it, but I have it at the back of my mind as a POSSIBILITY. MU, 10X in a year. What more do you want? Yeah, I know it has low PE, forward orders blah blah blah. They all look like that at tops. The most important question is, WHO ELSE is out there who needs to buy that hasn’t already bought? 
> - So, instead of continuing to buy / hold something that has POTENTIALLY topped, why not buy something else which has a higher probability of continuing the uptrend? Which is why the portfolio started to shift about 2-3 weeks ago into these other stocks. You will notice it if you have been copying my port for a while. In Apr and May, we were full of semiconductors, memory, photonics etc. Software in late May. And since then mainly the themes I talked about above. 
> - Other themes that are kindda standing out are consumer staples, quality stocks, financials, retail. This is why I am not totally bearish on the market overall. Market is just rotating to other sectors at the moment, NOT leaving the market totally. I don't see outright panic selling (though you might feel differently if you are holding all the previously hot stocks like AMD, INTC, AMAT, SNDK, MU, WDC, ALAB, MRVL, AAOI, LITE). 
> - One small tell is worth mentioning. WULF announced a major deal with Anthropic yesterday and gapped up at the open by about 17%? It sold off through the day, and today took out the deal announcement low as well as the prior day low! News and REACTION like this is very important for me. Remember I talked about how WDC could not hold the good news from MU? That was one canary in the coal mine. Then MU could not hold. Then Samsung. And WULF. ALL the hardware names simply could not catch a bid from good news. And if stocks cannot go up on good news, what do you expect them to do? There's only one other direction from there…
> - So, for me, I am avoiding most of the AI hardware players for now. And focusing on the DATABASE and SECURITY related players going forward. 
> - Just my 2 cents. Could be wrong. DYOR. NFA.

### Con (@__Con_)
_Tue Jul 07 21:45:45 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 66 · ↻ 3 · 💬 9 · [open on X](https://x.com/__Con_/status/2074610847473668106)

> Everyone's thinking the same thing here: "what's happening to AI stocks?"
>
> So, I'll explain what I think is happening.
>
> And where I see us moving forward.
>
> Let's deep dive:
>
> I think most of these are going through a "distribution" formation.
>
> Check the $SIVE chart below for what this means.
>
> But basically, we have a sell off here, until we start accumulating (or showing signs of higher highs, and a it being a good spot people bid at).
>
> Now we do have some fundamental reasons for this: 
>
> Firstly, SemiAnalysis wrote a piece on CPO delays and company valuations. 
>
> This caused the first sell off. 
>
> $NVDA and other optical companies refuted these claims, though.
>
> Secondly, we had a "sell the news" event on earnings and expections. 
>
> $MU and Samsung's recent earning results were very strong, but it seems to not have been the massive beating investors were hoping for. 
>
> So, this triggered sharp drops in memory and chip stocks ($MU, $SNDK, etc.), spilling over to the broader sector. Investors had priced in perfection.
>
> I mean, check the past chart growth when this is really priced in for future growth % potential. 
>
> Thirdly, we've had some "is this a bubble" fears.
>
> AI infrastructure spending is enormous (hyperscalers like $MSFT , $GOOGL, $META, $AMZN on track for hundreds of billions), but questions linger on the short-term ROI. Is this sustainable?
>
> Especially with the $META renting out $NBIS compute. 
>
> People think it shows $META might not need as much compute in the future. So we saw a mass sell off on some names: $NBIS, $BRUN, $IREN, $HIVE, etc., but I don't think this will last.
>
> I wrote about this earlier (just look at my earlier posts on $NBIS).
>
> And enablers (such as $NVDA, $AMD, $AVGO, $MU, photonics plays like $SIVE, optical interconnects, power/cooling) ran up hugely on the buildout narrative. Profit-taking + rotation out of "expensive" tech is natural after crazy pumps (natural human psychology imo).
>
> Fourth, we got some macro pressures holding us down (not limited to these companies, but they hurt the risk-on ones most): 
>
> Interest rates/inflation: Fears of higher rates (Fed outlook, oil prices from geopolitics like Iran-related tensions) raise borrowing costs for the capital-intensive AI buildout. Debt financing for data centers and infra is surging too, so that doesn't help.
>
> Geopolitical noise and strong jobs data have added volatility as well.
>
> And lastly, as I'm writing this, news just broke out that the U.S. has started launching strikes against Iran again... so that's an added confluence we needed lol.
>
> But, soon, I think we'll getting into the classic accumulation zone.
>
> I think the $BTC -> AI pivot companies will hold best here, as crypto has bottomed imo.
>
> But for the rest, I think we have a bit lower to go. Maybe just a tad.
>
> In particular, $NBIS has a clear zone at 170 that I'm looking at for support. I'm hoping it holds there and accumulates for a bit before sending higher.
>
> For $OPTX, I think this is in a consolidation phase, and $ASYS as well.
>
> This really applies to all of these stocks (even $AAOI, $CRWV, and any other one you can think of).
>
> We accumulate here before sending higher.
>
> It's not going to be the "V" shape you all know and love.
>
> But with due time, we will go up again imo.

### cryptid (@wetyeti01)
_Tue Jul 07 23:18:47 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 2 · ↻ 0 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/wetyeti01/status/2074634262603850165)

> Fascinating breakthrough from Osaka Metropolitan University on this phase-change magneto-optical metagrating device! Steering heat non-reciprocally at near-straight-on angles, separating absorption/emission, switching with GST, storing states power-free, and tuning via magnetic fields is huge for thermal photonics.
> Here’s a speculative systems-level concept building directly on it for future high-performance 3D chip stacks (AI accelerators, HPC, etc.):
> Hierarchical “Thermo-Magnetic Intelligent Packaging” Architecture
> Chip-level (micro): Integrate small metagratings on the backside or edges of compute dies. Waste heat naturally drives resonant mid-IR (~13μm) emission. GST enables on/off latching of nonreciprocity; magnetic field provides continuous spectral/frequency tuning and steering. Modulated incoherent IR carries:
> •  Operational control logic
> •  Thermal status/hotspot data
> •  Commands for dynamic management
> •  Low-speed sideband/backup memory (non-urgent data, configs, logs, checkpoints)
> This keeps the main silicon cores 100% dedicated to high-speed data processing—no control overhead.
> Macro control level (package/board): A distributed network of Ni/Ti (Nitinol) elements handles global orchestration:
> •  Automated feedback loops for thermal balancing across the entire stack.
> •  Excess heat removal via actuated/curved paths through insulating seals to sinks.
> •  Structural support and mechanical stability for the 3D assembly.
> •  Field producers: Ni/Ti wires/structures generate or modulate the required transverse magnetic fields (~1T regionally) to steer the chip-level IR emission without placing magnets directly on delicate silicon.
> •  Multi-tasking sensors (temperature via resistance/shape response) + electrical switching.
> How it works in operation:
> •  Chips generate heat → metagratings modulate and directionally steer IR (short-range only: mm to cm, as far as needed for local heat removal).
> •  IR signal travels to macro detectors or adjacent layers, carrying control data.
> •  Macro Ni/Ti network senses globally, actuates heat routing, adjusts magnetic fields for optimal steering, and balances load/heat across the stack in real time.
> •  Closed-loop, low-power (non-volatile GST + shape-memory states), self-aware thermal management.
> Benefits:
> •  Turns waste heat into a useful control + sideband communication medium.
> •  Massive parallelism (many extraction paths per chip/layer) boosts effective bandwidth for control traffic.
> •  Clean separation: Compute optimized for speed; thermal/control offloaded to the “heat fabric.”
> •  Improved resilience, predictive maintenance, and efficiency in dense 3D stacks.
> •  Scalable with existing advanced packaging (interposers, hybrid bonding).
> This isn’t a near-term product—just an extrapolation showing how your device’s nonreciprocal heat steering + non-volatile switching could enable truly intelligent, heat-utilizing systems. No extra laser heat bleed; everything rides on waste heat management.
> What do you think—any other applications for programmable thermal radiation like this in sensors, energy harvesting, or photonics? Great work by the team! @OsakaMetUniv_en @physorg_com

### FrencHorizon (@FrencHorizon6)
_Tue Jul 07 23:25:29 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/FrencHorizon6/status/2074635947619041379)

> Semiconductor & photonics names across the list took a broad hit today, with the Philadelphia Semiconductor Index shedding over 5% following a classic "sell-the-news" reaction to Samsung's record Q2 earnings — a 19-fold surge in operating profit that still fell short of elevated expectations, triggering aggressive profit-taking across AI-linked chip and optical stocks. Morgan Stanley's call to reduce semiconductor exposure and DeepSeek's reported development of an in-house AI inference chip added further headwinds to the sector.
>
> AXT Inc.  was among the hardest hit, dropping -8.5% to $58.15 on elevated volume of over 8.3M shares. The pullback follows Monday's +19% two-day surge driven by a landmark $22.3M prepaid supply agreement with Coherent — that deal's fundamentals remain intact, and Northland Capital holds an Outperform rating with a $125 price target, but today's move reflects broader sector rotation rather than company-specific deterioration. Notably, AXTI still trades well off its 52-week high of $143.16, underscoring the volatility inherent in this high-beta AI wafer play.
> Coherent Corp.  shed -6.4% to $314.13, giving back recent gains despite a strong fundamental backdrop — FQ3 revenue of $1.81B (+21% YoY), a $2B NVIDIA investment, and a Wall Street median price target of $372.50 all suggest the selloff is valuation-driven rather than thesis-breaking. Applied Optoelectronics  fell -7.3% to $114.41, compounded by mixed analyst sentiment (consensus Hold) and notable insider selling of over 500,000 shares in the past quarter. Sive  and 0ND2.L  also declined sharply at -11.7% and -12.7% respectively, consistent with the broader risk-off tone hitting smaller-cap names hardest.
>
> The overarching theme is a multi-day whipsaw in AI hardware and semiconductor supply chain stocks — last week's selloff, Monday's partial rebound, and today's renewed pressure illustrate how sensitive these names remain to macro sentiment shifts around AI capex sustainability.

> No blind chasing here.

### Ren (@ren_stocks)
_Tue Jul 07 23:48:53 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 313 · ↻ 37 · 💬 15 · [open on X](https://x.com/ren_stocks/status/2074641836874809650)

> Scale-out CPO switches going from 5,000 units this year to 200,000 by 2030. And you are selling?
>
> That’s a 144% CAGR. A 40x volume ramp that both Yole and Morgan Stanley are modeling off the same wall. That’s the whole thesis, and notice what it doesn’t require: it doesn’t require me to pick which laser vendor qualifies into which switch, or whether Broadcom’s socket beats Nvidia’s.
>
> To be short this ramp up you have to argue the entire build doesn’t happen, and good luck making that case while the SemiAnalysis “delay” everyone panicked over still lands you at 200k units by 2030. 
>
> A delay bends the curve doesn’t make it go away. 
>
> The physics won’t let it go away. A 200,000 GPU cluster is burning ~17 megawatts just on transceivers. CPO cuts that ~73% per 800G. At scale-up density copper is already dead and pluggables are out of runway. Forced migrations are the best ramps you can be long because the demand doesn’t care.
>
> The biggest winners:
>
> Lasers and light sources: $LITE, $COHR, $SIVE
> Optical engines and pump lasers: $AAOI, $COHR
> Switch ASICs: $AVGO, $MRVL, $NVDA
> Optical I/O chiplets: $ALAB, $CRDO
> Packaging and assembly: $FN, $AMKR
> InP substrate and materials: $AXTI
>
> LITE is the cleanest CPO scarcity play, shipping 200G-per-lane EMLs at volume, book through 2028. $AAOI is the one that wins both ways: its core 800G and 1.6T pluggable business actually benefits if CPO slips, while its external laser fab keeps it in the game when CPO finally ramps.
>
> Bullish photonics ⚡️

### GUL (@gulVasikova)
_Wed Jul 08 18:04:13 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 2 · ↻ 0 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/gulVasikova/status/2074917486324314306)

> 🇨🇦 Canada is quietly becoming one of the world’s biggest quantum computing hubs, and investors are starting to pay attention.
>
> For years, Canada invested heavily in quantum research while much of the market focused on AI. Now that companies like $NVDA are openly embracing quantum computing, investors are beginning to realize that Canada may already have one of the strongest quantum ecosystems outside the U.S.
>
> Since 2002, Canada has invested more than $2 billion into quantum technology, while the government recently committed another $334 million to accelerate development. That funding isn’t just supporting research—it’s helping build an entire industry spanning hardware, software, cybersecurity, networking, and future AI infrastructure.
>
> One of the biggest names is $XNDU (Xanadu Quantum Technologies), which recently became Canada’s first publicly traded pure-play quantum computing company.
>
> Unlike many competitors building superconducting quantum computers, Xanadu is developing photonic quantum computers, which use light (photons) instead of electrical circuits. Many researchers believe photonics could eventually offer better scalability, lower cooling requirements, and easier integration into future AI data centers.
>
> Canada’s strength extends well beyond one company.
>
> Companies like $BTQ, Quantum eMotion, Photonic, Nord Quantique, and Quantum Technologies are all building different pieces of the future quantum ecosystem, from post-quantum cybersecurity to fault-tolerant quantum hardware.
>
> A major validation came when DARPA, the U.S. Defense Advanced Research Projects Agency, selected several Canadian quantum startups for its Quantum Benchmarking Initiative. DARPA is looking for technologies capable of building commercially useful quantum computers by 2033.
>
> That recognition suggests Canadian companies are competing on a global stage—not just in academic research.
>
> Why is $XNDU heavily shorted?
>
> Despite the excitement, $XNDU currently has one of the highest short interests in the market, with over 70% of its free float sold short.
>
> Short sellers believe the company’s valuation has moved far ahead of today’s business fundamentals. Revenue remains relatively small, profitability is still years away, and commercial quantum computing is still in its early stages.
>
> Their argument is simple:
>
> “The technology is promising—but investors may be paying tomorrow’s price for a company that is still building today’s products.”
>
> However, the opposite argument is equally compelling.
>
> If $XNDU continues hitting technical milestones, signs major commercial partnerships, or demonstrates meaningful progress toward scalable quantum computing, that extremely high short interest could fuel a powerful short squeeze, forcing bearish investors to buy back shares at much higher prices.
>
> Wall Street remains constructive despite the volatility, with analysts maintaining a Moderate Buy rating and an average price target implying roughly 275% upside from recent trading levels.
>
> The bigger picture
>
> Think about AI 15 years ago.
>
> Back then, most AI companies generated little revenue and many looked expensive. Investors who focused only on current earnings often missed the enormous opportunity that followed.
>
> Quantum computing could be following a similar path.
>
> Today it’s still experimental.
>
> Over the next decade, it could transform drug discovery, financial modeling, materials science, cybersecurity, climate simulation, and AI itself.
>
> There will likely be winners and losers along the way, but Canada has quietly positioned itself as one of the global leaders in this race.
>
> For long-term investors, the real question isn’t whether quantum computing will matter.
>
> It’s which companies will become the Nvidia, TSMC, or Microsoft of the quantum era. $XNDU is one of the companies trying to earn that position, making it one of the more closely watched—and most controversial—quantum stocks in the market today.

- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HMuWdF9awAAW5gk.jpg

### 투자/주식의 생활화 퇴직 오과장 (@datastaion)
_Wed Jul 08 18:45:37 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 5 · ↻ 0 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/datastaion/status/2074927905860427952)

> AI 사이클 내년이후로 길게보면
> 엔비디아 TSMC 브로드컴
> 지표기업들
> 컴퓨팅파워와 속도 네트워킹.
> ㅡㅡㅡㅡㅡ
>
> [뉴스] TSMC의 PIC 생산 능력, 2028년까지 월 25,000장으로 급증 전망; 엔비디아와 브로드컴이 초기 COUPE 고객으로 거론됨
>
> TSMC가 실리콘 포토닉스(Silicon Photonics) 분야로 사업을 확장하면서 시장의 관심이 쏠리고 있는 가운데, PIC(광집적회로, Photonic Integrated Circuits) 웨이퍼 생산 능력이 대폭 확대될 것으로 예상됩니다. 상업시보(Commercial Times)에 따르면, 기관 투자자들은 TSMC의 PIC 생산 능력이 월 약 500장 수준에서 2026년 2분기 10,000장으로 늘어나고, 4분기에는 15,000장으로 추가 확대되며, 2028년에는 월 최소 25,000장에 달할 것으로 추산하고 있습니다.
>
> 해당 보도에서 강조했듯, 초기 생산 램프업(생산량 확대) 기간 동안에는 PIC 생산 능력이 제한적이기 때문에 2026~2027년 TSMC의 COUPE 플랫폼 양산을 이용할 주요 고객은 엔비디아(NVIDIA), 브로드컴(Broadcom), AMD가 될 가능성이 높습니다. 2028년에 생산 능력이 더욱 확대되면, 미디어텍(MediaTek), 마벨(Marvell), 아야 랩스(Ayar Labs) 등 고객사의 CPO(공동 패키지 광학, Co-Packaged Optics) 프로젝트 역시 TSMC의 양산 플랫폼에 진입할 수 있을 것으로 보입니다.
>
> PIC는 전기 및 광 신호를 변환, 라우팅, 결합하는 역할을 담당합니다. AI 서버 클러스터가 지속적으로 확장되고 스위치 대역폭이 25T 및 50T에서 100T 및 200T로 고도화됨에 따라 광 엔진에 대한 수요도 증가하고 있으며, 이에 따라 TSMC의 COUPE 플랫폼 진행 상황이 시장의 주요 관심사가 되고 있다고 보도는 덧붙였습니다.
>
> 이 보도에 따르면, 웨이퍼당 648개의 다이(die)가 생산된다고 가정할 때, TSMC의 월간 PIC 생산 능력이 500장에서 10,000장으로 늘어나면 연간 PIC 생산량은 약 400만 개에서 7,800만 개로 급증하게 됩니다. 생산 능력이 월 25,000장으로 더욱 확대될 경우, 연간 PIC 생산량은 약 1억 9,400만 개에 달할 수 있습니다.
>
> 이러한 전망을 바탕으로, 해당 보도는 TSMC의 PIC 생산 능력 확대가 갖는 세 가지 주요 시사점을 강조합니다.
>
> 1. CPO의 양산 진입: 
> CPO 기술이 실험 및 소량 검증 단계를 넘어 점차 대량 생산 준비 단계로 나아가고 있음을 의미합니다.
>
> 2. 포괄적 AI 플랫폼 구축: 
> 실리콘 포토닉스와 첨단 패키징(Advanced Packaging)의 결합을 통해 COUPE, SoIC, CoWoS를 모두 결합한 더욱 포괄적인 AI 광전(optoelectronic) 플랫폼이 구축될 것으로 예상됩니다.
>
> 3. 관련 장비 수요 증가: 
> PIC 생산량이 증가함에 따라 광섬유 어레이 유닛(FAU), 레이저, 광학 테스트 장비, 프로브 카드(Probe cards), 테스트 소켓 및 자동화 장비에 대한 수요를 견인할 것으로 예상됩니다.
>
> 상용화를 향해 나아가는 TSMC의 COUPE 플랫폼
> 경제일보(Economic Daily News)의 보도처럼, TSMC는 자사의 COUPE 플랫폼을 기반으로 한 세계 최초의 200Gbps 마이크로 링 변조기(MRM, Micro-Ring Modulator)가 2026년 하반기에 양산에 들어갈 예정이라고 발표했습니다. 
> 또한 TSMC는 이 소자가 공정 제어 조건 하에서 1E-08 미만의 비트 에러율(Bit Error Rate)을 달성했다고 밝혔습니다.
>
> 그러나 상업시보는 PIC 생산 능력 증가가 곧바로 CPO의 대규모 양산 램프업을 의미하는 것은 아니라고 지적합니다. 
>
> 다운스트림(후공정) 프로세스가 완성되기 위해서는 SoIC 통합, 광전 테스트, 광 엔진 패키징, FAU 결합, 시스템 수준의 검증 등 여러 단계를 아직 통과해야 하기 때문입니다.
>
> https://t.co/w4FQ8IuzkB

>
> 🇵🇱 GPW: Duża nerwowość, mała zmiana na zamknięciu 🦅
> Na zamknięciu WIG20 spadł symbolicznie o 0,05%, szeroki WIG stracił 0,06%, a sWIG80 zniżkował o 0,47%. Najlepiej zachował się mWIG40, który wzrósł o 0,23%.
>
> Obroty były wysokie i wyniosły 2,45 mld zł, z czego ponad 2 mld zł przypadło na WIG20. Największy handel koncentrował się na KGHM, Allegro, Orlenie i PKO BP. To była sesja dużych spółek i dużych emocji 💰.
>
> Orlen korzysta z drogiej ropy: Liderem WIG20 został Orlen (+3,51%). Skok cen ropy natychmiast poprawił sentyment do paliwowego giganta. W tle inwestorzy wyceniali ryzyko kolejnych problemów z transportem surowca przez Cieśninę Ormuz ⛽📈.
>
> Banki pomagają indeksowi: Dobrze wyglądały też Alior (+1,38%), Pekao (+1,34%) i PKO BP (+1,22%). To ważne, bo dziś RPP zgodnie z oczekiwaniami utrzymała stopy procentowe bez zmian, ze stopą referencyjną na poziomie 3,75%. Rynek dostał więc pauzę, a nie zaskoczenie 🏦.
>
> Allegro i Dino po zielonej stronie: W drugiej części sesji popyt pojawił się także na Allegro (+0,76%) i Dino (+0,80%). To pomogło WIG20 ograniczyć skalę spadku, mimo mocnej przeceny kilku ciężkich komponentów indeksu 🛒.
>
> KGHM głównym hamulcem: Największym problemem GPW był dziś KGHM (-6,69%). Spółce ciążyły spadki miedzi i srebra, a inwestorzy nadal trawią nową strategię 2055+. Rynek coraz uważniej patrzy na możliwe wyższe nakłady inwestycyjne i potencjalne transakcje M&A ⛏️📉.
>
> Budimex i przemysł pod presją: Słabo wypadł Budimex (-3,70%), a pod kreską znalazły się też Kęty (-1,74%) i Modivo (-1,49%). Bez wsparcia Orlenu i banków WIG20 wyglądałby dziś znacznie gorzej.
>
> Szeroki rynek z kilkoma mocnymi historiami: W mWIG40 świetnie poradziły sobie Inter Cars (+5,50%), Creotech (+4,56%) i Text (+4,21%). Creotech pomógł pozytywny komunikat o uzyskaniu łączności z satelitą Mikroglob-1, a Text kontynuował dobrą passę po wcześniejszych pozytywnych impulsach analitycznych 🚀.
>
> Po słabszej stronie znalazły się Polimex Mostostal (-4,96%), Lubawa (-3,94%), Rainbow (-3,66%) i Ten Square Games (-3,50%). W sWIG80 uwagę przyciągał Huuuge (-3,64%) po słabszych danych o przychodach za II kwartał, a pozytywnie wyróżniło się VIGO Photonics (+1,85%) po rekordowych kwartalnych przychodach.
>
> 🇺🇸 Wall Street: Ropa straszy Dow, chipy ratują Nasdaq 🇺🇸
> Za oceanem nastroje były nerwowe. Dow Jones tracił ponad 1%, S&P 500 był pod kreską, a Nasdaq zdołał odrobić część strat i krążył blisko poziomu odniesienia. To pokazuje, że rynek nie sprzedawał wszystkiego po równo. Największy ciężar spadł na sektory wrażliwe na wzrost cen ropy i rentowności.
>
> Przemysł i materiały pod presją: Najsłabiej wyglądały spółki przemysłowe i materiałowe. Droższa ropa to wyższe koszty transportu, produkcji i finansowania, więc inwestorzy szybko zaczęli ciąć ekspozycję na bardziej cykliczne segmenty rynku 🏭📉.
>
> Linie lotnicze i rejsy dostają cios: Wzrost cen paliwa uderzył też w spółki turystyczne i transportowe. United Airlines i Delta były pod presją, a operatorzy rejsów, tacy jak Carnival i Norwegian Cruise Line, również mocno traciły ✈️🚢.
>
> Chipy po lepszej stronie rynku: Ciekawie wyglądały półprzewodniki. Broadcom mocno rósł po informacji, że Apple planuje wydać ponad 30 mld USD w ramach umowy dotyczącej dostaw chipów. Nvidia również była na plusie po doniesieniach, że Chiny mogą dopuścić ograniczone zakupy chipów H200 przez największe lokalne firmy AI 🤖💻.
>
> To ważna zmiana po ostatnich dniach nerwowości. AI trade nadal jest chwiejny, ale nie został porzucony. Rynek po prostu coraz ostrzej rozróżnia spółki z konkretnymi kontraktami od tych, które rosną głównie na narracji.
>
> 🌍 Europa: Czerwień na Starym Kontynencie 🇪🇺
> Europa zareagowała na eskalację znacznie słabiej niż GPW. W momencie zamknięcia handlu w Warszawie niemiecki DAX tracił ponad 2%, podobnie słabo wyglądał francuski CAC 40, a brytyjski FTSE 100 spadał o ok. 1,7%.
>
> Warszawa na tym tle była relatywnie mocna. Pomogła struktura WIG20: drożejący Orlen, odbicie banków i popyt na kilka dużych spółek zrównoważyły mocny spadek KGHM. W Europie takiego bufora było mniej 🇪🇺⚖️.
>
> 💱 Waluty, obligacje i Fed: Ropa podbija inflacyjne obawy 💵
> Na rynku długu zrobiło się nerwowo. Rentowność amerykańskich 10-latek wzrosła w okolice 4,56%, a 30-latek przekroczyła 5%. To reakcja na drożejącą ropę i obawy, że kolejny szok energetyczny może utrudnić Fedowi walkę z inflacją.
>
> Do tego doszły minutes z czerwcowego posiedzenia Fedu. Zapiski pokazały podzielony obraz: część członków widzi argumenty za podwyżką stóp, choć na ostatnim posiedzeniu poparła jeszcze utrzymanie ich bez zmian. Rynek dostał więc sygnał, że Fed pod wodzą Kevina Warsha nie zamierza szybko wracać do luźniejszej polityki 🏦.
>
> Dolar zyskiwał na statusie bezpiecznej przystani, a złoty pozostawał pod presją globalnego risk-off. W kraju głównym wydarzeniem była decyzja RPP, ale jej wpływ był ograniczony, bo brak zmiany stóp był szeroko oczekiwany.
>
> 🛢️ Ropa: Geopolityczna premia wraca z impetem ⛽
> Najważniejszy ruch dnia wydarzył się na ropie. Brent rósł w okolice 78-80 USD za baryłkę, a WTI przekraczała 73 USD. Rynek wyceniał ryzyko dalszej eskalacji po amerykańskich uderzeniach na Iran i wypowiedziach Trumpa o końcu porozumienia.
>
> Dodatkowym czynnikiem było cofnięcie licencji pozwalającej Iranowi na globalny eksport ropy. To zwiększyło obawy o dostępność surowca i przypomniało inwestorom, jak wrażliwy pozostaje rynek energii na każdy sygnał z Bliskiego Wschodu 🕊️⚠️.
>
> 💡 Wniosek dnia:
> Środowa sesja była lekcją odporności GPW. Globalnie dominował strach przed eskalacją konfliktu USA-Iran, skokiem cen ropy i powrotem inflacyjnej presji. Europa mocno traciła, Wall Street była pod presją, a rentowności obligacji rosły.
>
> Na tym tle Warszawa zachowała się bardzo solidnie. WIG20 niemal odrobił silną poranną przecenę dzięki Orlenowi, bankom, Allegro i Dino. Z drugiej strony tak głęboki spadek KGHM pokazuje, że rynek pozostaje bardzo selektywny i karze spółki, przy których pojawiają się jednocześnie presja surowcowa oraz obawy o przyszłe wydatki inwestycyjne.
>
> Teraz najważniejsze będą trzy pytania: czy eskalacja wokół Iranu okaże się tylko kolejnym epizodem, czy początkiem większego kryzysu; czy ropa utrzyma się przy wyższych poziomach; oraz jak rynek zinterpretuje bardziej jastrzębie sygnały z Fedu. Jeśli ropa dalej będzie rosła, temat inflacji bardzo szybko wróci na pierwsze strony rynkowej agendy.
>

### Just2Trade (@Just2Trade)
_Wed Jul 08 19:30:09 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 1 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/Just2Trade/status/2074939113703145957)

> 🔬 Hawking Radiation — No Longer Just Theory?
>
> Stephen Hawking predicted that black holes slowly evaporate by emitting radiation — but testing this in space remains impossible. Now, physicists have experimentally studied the *backreaction* of stimulated Hawking radiation using an optical analogue — a lab-based system mimicking a black hole's event horizon with light and fiber optics. This is a landmark step: not just detecting analogue Hawking radiation, but observing how it *affects the system that produced it*. Understanding backreaction is crucial to resolving one of physics' deepest puzzles — the black hole information paradox. Lab-scale black hole mimics are becoming powerful tools for probing quantum gravity.
>
> #HawkingRadiation #QuantumPhysics #BlackHoles #AnalogueGravity #QuantumOptics
>
> ---
>
> Companies in this space: Coherent Corp. ($COHR, NYSE), II-VI / Coherent Advanced Photonics ($IIVI, NASDAQ), MKS Instruments ($MKSI, NASDAQ)

### Signe Plan (@AnetteO11)
_Wed Jul 08 21:35:37 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 1 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/AnetteO11/status/2074970687903563891)

> AMD is not alone or necessarily the first to market in an exclusive way, but they are very much in the race. Ayar Labs has secured major investments, with AMD Ventures, NVIDIA, and Intel Capital all contributing heavy multi-million dollar sums. All three giants are after the same thing: replacing traditional copper cables inside and between AI processors with light signals (optical I/O) to build ultra-fast AI supercomputers.
>
> 2. What is SuperNova?
>
> SuperNova is an external light source (a type of multi-laser device) that sends light across up to 16 different wavelengths through thin fiber-optic cables. Instead of sending electricity through copper, data is transmitted at the speed of light. This provides vastly higher bandwidth, lower latency, and consumes significantly less power, which is exactly what future, massive AI models require.
>
> 3. The Sivers Connection
>
> There is actually an interesting Swedish angle here: it is the semiconductor company Sivers Semiconductors through its subsidiary Sivers Photonics that has developed and delivered the advanced laser arrays used inside Ayar Labs' SuperNova modules.
>
> AMD is at the absolute forefront, integrating this technology into its future chip designs, but they share the pie and the technology with their biggest competitors Nvidia and Intel, who are also deeply involved with Ayar Labs.

> The Big Five are spending on AI faster than they're earning: @Microsoft, @Google, @amazon, @Meta. If CapEx exceeds cash flow, it can only persist as long as investors keep funding it. @PeterDiamandis asked me: What happens if sentiment shifts?
>
> Here's my take: sentiment won’t shift. If anything, the investment will become more justified over time.
>
> The world still sees compute as a rapidly depreciating asset but that’s simply not what it is anymore. Short of a massive leap in photonics or quantum computing, GPUs will continue to be highly sought after and have a predictable service life. This is already turning GPUs hours into a commodity.
>
> Think about it like buying a house: when you buy a house, you finance it, and the house is collateral. In a world where compute becomes acceptable collateral, the hyperscalers could easily raise 10x to 100x on their cash flow in equity and debt, if they choose to.
>
> In reality, there’s a lot of investable dollars in the world that want to flow into AI but can’t. AI is still the largest wealth creation moment in the history of humankind.

### buzzberg.ai (@buzzberg_ai)
_Wed Jul 08 22:59:18 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/buzzberg_ai/status/2074991747940118838)

> Daily Buzzberg Alpha
>
> the tape isn't sending one macro signal. it's repricing a regime: geopolitical supply risk returning while ai capex becomes an earnings tailwind AND an inflation/rates risk at the same time.
>
> that combination kills generic beta and creates dispersion. the market has stopped paying for ai exposure or risk-on exposure — it's paying for contracted demand, validated supply-chain position, and balance-sheet capacity. it's punishing crowded trades where the thesis is intact but the holder base is impaired.
>
> the whole note reduces to one filter: contracts > stories.
>
> — where the asymmetry sits —
>
> $WYFI — cleanest setup in the neocloud wreckage. ~$1b+ contracted backlog vs ~$1.3b market cap, and nscale's $900m credit facility validates the counterparty. sold with the basket, priced like the contracts don't exist.
>
> $AVGO — the one ai print this week backed by a signed deal: apple's $30b+ agreement + $1.5b colorado buildout. validates the custom asic layer beyond gpu scarcity. revenue visibility, not vibes — and the cleaner read-through than $AAPL, which carries higher domestic cost and eu overhang.
>
> $ONDS — thesis tied to numbers, not narrative: path to ~$1b revenue by 2027, net-income inflection, sum-of-parts floor, q2 print as the catalyst.
>
> photonics — the under-the-surface one. inp substrates easing from "very tight" to "tight" isn't bearish — it lets downstream optical names convert interconnect demand into shipments. distinguish upstream bottleneck vs downstream qualification moats. $LITE $AAOI $COHR
>
> $RKLB — flow unusually specific: 200dma entry, ms overweight $105 pt, vertical-integration bull case. blue origin's $130b private raise now anchors every public space comp.
>
> — crowded, entry decayed —
>
> $PENG — textbook signal decay. real discovery a month ago (earnings beat, cxl exposure, nvidia ai factory partner). now the flow is victory laps and partial trims. thesis quality high, entry quality gone.
>
> broad ai beta — warsh's divided fomc tied ai capex to upside inflation risk, some members already floating hikes. that's the mechanism: the buildout that feeds suppliers also keeps real rates sticky, so long-duration ai without contract visibility underperforms. $TLT stays exposed.
>
> — battleground —
>
> memory — highest-dispersion area on the tape. korean flow reads the samsung/hynix selloff as forced deleveraging (levered-etf + retail-credit mechanics, adr re-rating catalyst) with hbm4/rubin demand structural through 2028. us flow is chaos — "memory is dead" next to aggressive $MU $SNDK dip buys. right framing: thesis intact, ownership base damaged. tradable, not clean.
>
> oil — the move isn't the crude print, it's the transmission. brent ~$80 is the tactical level where short-covering extends, but the real signal is hormuz uncertainty leaking into diesel, propane, shipping and reserves — inflation pass-through that survives even if front-month crude stalls. own the complex where the physical market stays tight. $USO $CRAK
>
> also on the desk: $NBIS washed-out sub-$170 but the bar is now contracted utilization, $META's $10b canada dc arguing against a capex stop, $OUST physical-ai perception via nvidia jetson, $HOOD chain optionality (early, distribution call not revenue).
>
> bottom line: the tape is moving from "ai trade" to "ai underwriting." it pays receipts and punishes stories — $AVGO and $WYFI have them, $PENG had them last month, memory has them for 2028 but not for this week.

### Dan Coté (@DanCote303)
_Wed Jul 08 23:45:34 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 9 · ↻ 2 · 💬 3 · [open on X](https://x.com/DanCote303/status/2075003388346147121)

> Be warned!! This is a little long but VERY informative on who Kopin should be prospecting and timeline of execution.
>
> I KNOW we are early on $KOPN with its new MicroLED Neural I/o chip design. And its DEMO to be presented end of 2026. So trying to take advantage while their is time, #KOPIN should be looking into hyperscalers first. 
>
> Hyperscalers & Cloud AI Builders (Top Priority)
>
> NVIDIA (GPU clusters, NVLink complements), Google (TPUs), Amazon (Trainium/Inferentia), Microsoft (Azure Maia/custom silicon), Meta, Oracle, xAI, and others building massive AI training/inference clusters.
>
> WHY? 
> They face acute power and bandwidth walls in dense GPU racks. Power/cooling is a top TCO driver; Neural I/o promises major efficiency gains for intra-rack or short inter-rack GPU-to-GPU and GPU-to-memory traffic.
> AI Chip/Accelerator Designers
> NVIDIA, AMD, Broadcom (custom ASICs), and startups (Cerebras, Groq, SambaNova, etc.). Also advanced packaging players (TSMC, Intel, Samsung) for chiplet or co-packaged optics (CPO) integration.
>
> WHY? 
> Direct integration into next-gen accelerators or 2.5D/3D packages. Supports high-parallelism needs without heavy SerDes bottlenecks.
>
> Server/System OEMs & Integrators Supermicro, Dell, HPE, Lenovo.
>
> WHY? 
> They build the racks/servers sold to hyperscalers. Better interconnects enable higher-density, lower-power systems that differentiate their offerings. Networking & Photonics Ecosystem Broadcom (AVGO—networking ASICs/optics leader), Arista, Cisco, plus photonics firms (Lumentum/LITE, Coherent). Potential partners or complementors rather than pure competitors for specific short-reach use cases.
>
> Defense, Government & Sovereign AI Infrastructure
>
> DoD/intelligence community data centers, contractors, and sovereign AI projects (Europe, Middle East, Asia) seeking secure/domestic supply chains.
>
> WHY?
> Kopin’s US-based full MicroLED production capability + long defense heritage (displays, soldier systems) provides a strong moat for secure AI hardware. Dual-use potential with existing defense MicroLED work.
>
> Advantages of $KOPN vs. Current Data Center Interconnects
>
> Neural I/o sits in a “sweet spot” between copper’s limitations and traditional laser optics’ drawbacks for short-to-medium reach, high-bandwidth AI intra-cluster links. It draws from “wide-and-slow” parallel channel concepts (hundreds/thousands of lower-speed MicroLED channels instead of a few ultra-high-speed lanes), similar to Microsoft Research’s MOSAIC project (which demonstrated ~56-68% lower power, up to 50m reach, and much higher reliability using MicroLEDs + imaging fiber).Neural I/o wins on bandwidth scalability (parallelism enables 1.6 Tbps demo target soon, 3.6 Tbps roadmap), dramatically lower power per bit, less heat (easier cooling, higher rack density), and better reach for board/rack scales. It “breaks the copper wall” while keeping costs and power closer to copper-like economics for these reaches.Vs. Traditional Optical (InP/VCSEL lasers, silicon photonics transceivers, pluggable optics or CPO):
> Lasers excel at longer reach but are power-hungry, expensive, thermally sensitive, complex (heavy DSP, CDR, FEC, equalization, SerDes), and overkill (plus higher failure rates) for many short intra-rack or chip-to-chip links in AI clusters. They add cost, power, and complexity where not fully needed.
>
> Neural I/o wins by using MicroLEDs as direct emitters (cheaper, lower power, more temperature-robust, simpler drive electronics possible with parallel low-speed channels). It eliminates or reduces need for expensive laser modules and complex digital backends for targeted use cases. Potential for smaller form factor, higher reliability/redundancy (pixel-level), and better power efficiency (comparable to MOSAIC’s ~3-5W vs. 10-12W per link range in research). Bidirectional capability from NeuralDisplay architecture is a plus. It avoids “expensive laser-based systems entirely” for these applications while delivering needed bandwidth.
>
> LOOONG $KOPN

> Paradis Labs ยังมั่นใจ $AAOI และ $AEHR แม้หุ้น AI Small Cap ปรับฐานแรง
>
> Paradis Labs ระบุว่ายังคงถือหุ้น AAOI และ AEHR พร้อมแสดงความเชื่อมั่นต่อแนวโน้มระยะยาวของทั้งสองบริษัท แม้ว่าหุ้นกลุ่ม AI Infrastructure ขนาดเล็กจะถูกแรงขายกดดันในช่วงที่ผ่านมา
>
> สำหรับ AAOI มองว่า
>
> ตั้งเป้ารายได้จาก Optical Transceiver แตะประมาณ 471 ล้านดอลลาร์ต่อเดือนภายในกลางปี 2027
> บริษัทกำลังขยายกำลังการผลิตรองรับผลิตภัณฑ์ 800G และ 1.6T
> แม้เพิ่มกำลังผลิตแล้ว คาดว่าอุปสงค์จะยังสูงกว่ากำลังการผลิตจนถึงประมาณไตรมาส 3 ปี 2027
>
> ส่วน AEHR
>
> เพิ่งได้รับคำสั่งซื้อเพิ่มเติมสำหรับระบบ Wafer Level Burn-In (WLBI) จากลูกค้า Silicon Photonics
> มีโอกาสได้รับคำสั่งซื้อเพิ่มภายในปีนี้ หลังผ่านการรับรองเป็นซัพพลายเออร์แล้ว
> ก่อนหน้านี้ยังได้รับคำสั่งซื้อระบบ Package Level Burn-In (PLBI) จากลูกค้า Hyperscaler รายใหญ่
>
> Paradis Labs ระบุว่า หุ้นทั้งสองตัวมีความผันผวนสูง (High Beta) จึงถูกแรงขายในรอบ AI Selloff มากกว่าหุ้นขนาดใหญ่ แต่ยังเชื่อมั่นในแนวโน้มระยะยาวและยังคงถือการลงทุนต่อ

AAOI has explosive revenue growth actually materializing, on top of a surging **backlog**, whereas Sivers is baiting retail with a merely subjective **opportunity pipeline**, with zero photonics revenue today, let alone even a backlog to show for anything. And pricing power will be fully at the discretion of WIN Semi, who they outsource designs to, further eroding potential margins should anything even manifest. I mean hey, this thing could surely pump again, but the risks are IMMENSE and it will only run on hype, which is intrinsically fizzling out (especially with all this dilution and some serious macro risks on the horizon/liquidity tightening).
